Math Questions..Cross Products of Sets?



Math Questions..Cross Products of Sets?



1.Villiant Bank’s website requires that your pin number only be two numerical digits long. So, the first number to choose will be from set A below and the second number to choose will be from set B. Find the cross product A X B to determine the number of combinations possible. (4 points)



A = {0, 2, 4, 6, 8}



B = {1, 3, 5, 7, 9}



2.Vall ant Bank’s website requires that your pin number be two digits long, the first must be a V or B and the second a number from 1 to 5. So, the first digit to choose will be from set C below and the second digit to choose will be from set D. Find the cross product C X D to determine the number of combinations possible. (4 points)



C = {v, b}



D = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5}



3.Based on your answers from parts 1 & 2, what is the difference in the number of possible pin numbers between Genuine and Valliant Banks. Which would you be more comfortable using if you were concerned with identity theft? Why? Compose a short paragraph to explain.

2. A particular salad contains 4 units of vitamin A, 4 units of vitamin B-complex, and 3 mg of fat per serving. A
nutritious soup contains 6 units of vitamin A, 2 units of vitamin B-complex, and 3 mg fat per serving. If a lunch
consisting of these two foods is to have at least 10 units of vitamin A, and at least 10 units of vitamin B-complex,
how many servings of each food should be used to minimize the total milligrams of fat?

<question>



Math problem that has to do with %?



If high school graduates make 1.2mil in a life time and a college graduates make 2.1mil in a life time the college grads are making 75% more than the high school grads. then if a College grad had a job that he could make 2.1mil in his life time but only worked enough to make 1.2mil how much % less time would he be working than the high school grad?



Thanks



</question>



<answer from>



heelfan5...
Member since: 01 August 2008
Total points: 172 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



I'm sorry I did not know advances question plus I do not feel like I would want to read this question that now



</answer>



<answer from>



JoelKatz
Member since: 15 May 2008
Total points: 11565 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



If he could earn 2.1, but only works enough to earn 1.2, then he has skipped out on earning .9 of the 2.1 he could earn and thus .9 of the 2.1 work he could do. To convert this to a percentage, it's:
(.9/2.1) * 100 = 42.8%



So he does 42.8% less work.



</answer>



<answer from>



Robert S
Member since: 20 April 2007
Total points: 25961 (Level 7)



</answer from>



<answer>



42.8%



</answer>



<answer from>



x.lamour
Member since: 04 September 2008
Total points: 185 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



42.86%



</answer>



<answer from>



hellogoo...
Member since: 16 December 2006
Total points: 2194 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



1.2mil is 57.14% of 2.1mil ((1.2/2.1) * 100).



So the college grad would be working 100 - 57.14 = 42.86% less time.



</answer>

<question>



Factor completely



x*-5x-6?



algebra



</question>



<answer from>



King Lucario™
Member since: 08 April 2008
Total points: 7783 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



(x+1)(x-6)



Source(s):



Y! Answers Expert



</answer>



<answer from>



intellec...
Member since: 06 December 2007
Total points: 25761 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



x^2 - 5x - 6
= x^2 + x - 6x - 6
= (x^2 + x) - (6x + 6)
= x(x + 1) - 6(x + 1)
= (x + 1)(x - 6)



</answer>



<answer from>

Member since: 18 August 2008

<answer>



x^2 - 5x - 6
(x-6) (x+1)



</answer>

<question>



Mathematics Probability question. Can you help?



Hey.



I've recently done a recap on Probability and i'm having some problems. I've learnt difference between independent events and mututally exclusive events but i'm having trouble with answering some of these questions. There is the AND Rules and the OR Rule.



Can you explain a method of solving this question please.



1. Find the probability of picking 2 queens plus the ace of spades from a pack of cards (without replacement).



The answer in the book is 3/11050 but i get the answer of 1/11050 becuase i do 4/52 x 3/51 x 1/50. Why is it 3/11050?



All comments are very much appreciated. Many thanks!



</question>



<answer from>



Obama has my vote &lt;3
Member since: 18 September 2008
Total points: 465 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



there are 4 queens in the deck not only 2



</answer>



<answer from>



Madhukar Daftary
Member since: 17 January 2007
Total points: 33827 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Total number of ways of picking up 3 cards out of 52 cards is
n = 52C3



No. of ways of picking up an ace of spade and two queens
r = 1 x 4C2
=&gt; required probability
= r/n
= 4C2 / 52C3
= 6 / 22100
= 3 / 11050.



</answer>

<question>



Please help me with this problem?



what quadrant does -119 degrees and -167 degrees lie on?



is it in first quad?



</question>



<answer from>



kumorifo...
Member since: 29 June 2007
Total points: 21582 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Chemistry



</answer from>



<answer>



No, 3rd quadrant.



The positive values of these lie in the second quadrant. But because they are negative, you go in the reverse direction. Then, the second and third quadrants interchange.



Easier way: subtract the numerical value from 360 (i.e. 360-119, or 360-167), and check where those values would lie.



</answer>



<answer from>



JoeyMigs
Member since: 18 August 2008
Total points: 1243 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



both are in quadrant III



</answer>



<answer from>



Jason C
Member since: 08 August 2008
Total points: 189 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



..............|
......2......|........1
..............|



_______|_______
..............|
......3......|........4
..............|



negative 119 (-119) would mean you start from the line between 1 and 4 and move clockwise 119 degrees --&gt; end up in the 3rd quadrant.  Same with -167 degrees.



</answer>



<answer from>



Puzzling
Member since: 18 March 2006
Total points: 72800 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Each quadrant is 90°.



Going counter clockwise:
Quadrant I = 0° to 90°
Quadrant II = 90° to 180°
Quadrant III = 180° to 270°
Quadrant IV = 270° to 360°



Going clockwise:
Quadrant IV = 0° to -90°
Quadrant III = -90° to -180°
Quadrant II = -180° to -270°
Quadrant I = -270° to -360°



Both of your angles lie in Quadrant III



</answer>

<question>



Find the value of x (the pythagorean relation)?



http://i461.photobucket.com/albums/qq337...



click this to show the problem



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



According to Pythagorean theorem:
a^2 + b^2 = c^2



x = the unknown
a^2 + x^2 = 10^2 (&lt;== hypotenuse)
a^2 + x^2 = 100
8^2 + 6^2 = 100
64 + 36 = 100
100 = 100



∴ x = 6



</answer>

<question>



Solving equations help (8th grade advanced)?



My teache has a thig with yelling and does teach =/



1.) -2d + 18 - 4d = 60



2.) 3 (n+5) + 2 = 26



</question>



<answer from>



Jun Agruda
Member since: 17 May 2007
Total points: 29695 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



1st problem:
- 2d + 18 - 4d = 60
6d = - 42
d = - 7



Answer: d = - 7



Proof:
- 2(- 7) + 18 - 4(- 7) = 60
14 + 18 + 28 = 60
60 = 60



2nd problem:
3(n + 5) + 2 = 26
3n + 15 = 24
n + 5 = 8
n = 3



Answer: n = 3



Proof:
3(3 + 5) + 2 = 26
3(8) + 2 = 26
24 + 2 = 26
26 = 26



</answer>



<answer from>



intellec...
Member since: 06 December 2007
Total points: 25707 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



1)
-2d + 18 - 4d = 60
-2d - 4d = 60 - 18
-6d = 42
d = 42/-6
d = -7



2)
3(n + 5) + 2 = 26
3*n + 3*5 = 26 - 2
3n + 15 = 24
3n = 24 - 15
n = 9/3
n = 3



</answer>



<answer from>



I'm finished making sense
Member since: 03 September 2007
Total points: 1103 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



1.) -2d + 18 - 4d = 60 collect like terms
-6d + 18 = 60 subtract 18 from both sides
-6d = 42 divide by -6
d = -7



2.) 3 (n+5) + 2 = 26 expand the brackets
3n + 15 + 2 = 26 collect like terms
3n + 17 = 26 subtract 17 from both sides
3n = 9 divide by 3
n = 3



=)



Source(s):



Me!



</answer>



<answer from>



cathrl69
Member since: 10 July 2007
Total points: 18515 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



1) Combine the "d"s on one side of the equation and the numbers on the other, then multiply both sides by the same value such that you end up with "d =" and a number on the right. That would be the answer.



2) Exactly the same, except that it's n, and you'll need to multiply out the brackets first.



Just do the same thing on either side of the equals sign at every step.



I'm really struggling with this being considered "advanced" for a 13-14 year old. It's about as basic as algebra gets.



</answer>



<answer from>



Smile
Member since: 18 September 2008
Total points: 127 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



1 ) -2d + 18 - 4d = 60
-2d-4d = 60 - 18
-6d = 42
d = 42/-6
d = -42 / 6
d = -7



2) 3 (n+5) + 2 = 26
3 *n + 3 * 5 + 2 = 26
3 * n + 15 + 2 = 26
3 * n + 17 = 26
3 * n = 26 - 17
3 * n = 9
n = 9 / 3
n = 3



</answer>

<question>



Math problems!!! HELP!!!?



3 - (2 + 3x)



8d - (4d + 2)



5 + 4(5n - 3) - 5n



</question>



<answer from>



King Lucario™
Member since: 08 April 2008
Total points: 7789 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



3-(2+3x)
3-2-3x
1-3x



8d-(4d+2)
8d-4d-2
4d-2



5+4(5n-3)-5n
5+20n-12-5n
-7+15n



</answer>



<answer from>



intellec...
Member since: 06 December 2007
Total points: 25761 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



1)
3 - (2 + 3x)
= 3 - 2 - 3x
= 1 - 3x



2)
8d - (4d + 2)
= 8d - 4d - 2
= 4d - 2
= 2(2d - 1)



3)
5 + 4(5n - 3) - 5n
= 5 + 4*5n - 4*3 - 5n
= 5 + 20n - 12 - 5n
= 15n - 7



</answer>



<answer from>



Pranil
Member since: 02 March 2007
Total points: 24988 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



3 – (2 + 3x)
= 3 – 2 – 3x
= 1 – 3x



8d – (4d + 2)
= 8d – 4d – 2
= 4d – 2



5 + 4(5n – 3) – 5n
= 5 + 4×5n – 4×3 – 5n
= 5 + 20n – 12 – 5n
= 15n – 7
---------



</answer>

<answer>



1. (8 - 3) × 2 + (16 + 467) × 3
5(2)+483(3)
10+1449
1459
2. (898 - 1 × 14) × 27 ÷ 9 + 4
(898-14)(27)/9+4
884(27)/9+4
23868/9+4
2652+4
2656

<question from>



universa...

<question>



Show the sequence { x(subn) } n=1 to ∞?



Show the sequence { x(subn) } n=1 to ∞ is decreasing



x(sub n+1) = (1/2)[ x(subn) + a / x(subn) ] for all n, a &gt; 0



Tip: x(sub n+1) = average of x(subn) & a/x(subn)



</question>

</question from>



<question>



Maths Question Problem?



On Sat, there were 60 less male visitors than female visitors to a park.
On Sun, the number of male visitors increased by 30% while the number of female
visitors decreased by 10%.



If there were a total of 494 visitors on Sunday,
a) find the number of female visitors on Sun.
b) what was the total sum of money collected from the admission fees on both days if each admission ticket to the park cost $4?



</question>



<answer from>



Chris L
Member since: 24 September 2008
Total points: 438 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Let x be the male visitors on Saturday, and y be the female visitors on Saturday:



x + y = 494 (because there were 494 total)
y = x + 60 (because there were 60 more women than men)



If you substitute (x + 60) for y in the first equation, you have:
x + x + 60 = 494
2x + 60 = 494
2x = 434
x = 217



So, on Saturday, there were 217 men and 277 women.  On Sunday:
men went up 30% = 217 * 1.3 = 282
women went down 10% = 277 * 0.9 = 249



So, there were 531 total visitors on Sunday (282 men and 249 women).



To find the money collected, add up the totals from each day and multiply by $4:
(494 + 531) * 4 = 1025 * 4 = $4100



</answer>



<answer from>



Pranil
Member since: 02 March 2007
Total points: 24990 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Let there be x females on saturday. Then (x – 60) male on saturday
total visitors = x + x – 60 = 2x + 60
on sunday
female visitors = 0.9x amd male visitors 1.3(x – 60) = 1.3x – 78
total visitors on sunday = 0.9x + 1.3x – 78 = 494
2.2x = 572
x = 260 female on saturday
a) 0.9 × 260 = 234 female on sunday



visitors on saturday
female 260 and male 260 – 60 = 200
total on sunday = 260 + 200 = 460
total on sunday = 494
total on both days = 954
collection = 954 × 4 = $ 3816
--------



</answer>

<question>



Word problem ( 2 problem)?



1.) If the length of the diagonal of a rectangle is 50in. and the area is 1200m^2, what are the dimensions?



2.) What are the dimensions in ( problem 1) if the the length of diagonal is 13in. and the area is 60in^2



</question>



<answer from>



nottheja...
Member since: 13 February 2008
Total points: 16965 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



1)  if the diagonal is 50, then x^2 + y^2 = 50^2 (from Pythagoras)
from area, we know that xy = 1200, or y = 1200 / x



substituting in to the first equation:
x^2 + (1200 / x)^2 = 50^2 = 2500
x^2 + 1440000 / x^2 = 2500
x^4 + 1440000 = 2500 x^2
x^4 - 2500 x^2 + 1440000 = 0
(x^2 -1600)(x^2 - 900) = 0
so x = 40 or x = 30 (for positive values of x)



if x = 40, then y = 1200 / 40 = 30
if x = 30, then y = 1200 / 30 = 40



the dimensions are 30 by 40
(diagonal = 50 and area = 1200)



2)now the equations become:
x^2 + y^2 = 13^2 = 169
xy = 60, or y = 60/x
x^2 + (60/x)^2 = 169
x^4 + 3600 = 169x^2
x^4 - 169x^2 + 3600 = 0
(x^2 - 25)(x^2 - 144) = 0
x = 5 or x = 12 (for positive roots)



the rectangle is 5 by 12 (diagonal = 13 and area = 60)



</answer>



<answer from>



linlyons
Member since: 08 July 2006
Total points: 46687 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Global Warming

</answer from>



<answer>



nott is correct.  however, 3-4-5 and 5-12-13 are well known right triangles.



when i read the first problem, i wondered.
when i read the second, with diagonal of 13, i did the 5x12 multiplication in my head and got 60.



so the 2nd rectangle is 5x12  which has a 31 diagonal.



the first is 30x40 which has an area of 1200  and a diagonal of 50.



</answer>

<question>



What is the prime factorization of 648?



its math homework



can u please show the work



</question>



<answer from>



hayharbr
Member since: 12 February 2006
Total points: 65364 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Homework Help



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



648/2 = 324
324/2 = 162
162 / 2 = 81
81/3 = 27
27/3 = 9
9/3 = 3
3/3 = 1 which is not prime
so 3x3x3x3x2x2x2



</answer>



<answer from>



kumorifo...
Member since: 29 June 2007
Total points: 21592 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Chemistry



</answer from>



<answer>



First, divide by the smallest possible prime number (2).



2×324



Then, do it again, until you can no longer divide by that number.



2×2×162
2×2×2×81



Then, factorise the remaining numbers, if done easily, else divide by the next smallest prime number.



81 = 9×9, and 9 = 3×3



So 648 = 2×2×2×3×3×3×3



</answer>

f prime = [ (x-3) 1 - (x+5) 1] / (x-3)^2

enterrea...

<answer>



Let u = x + 5 and v = x - 3



(d/dx)(u/v) = [v(du/dx) - u(dv/dx)]/v^2



f'(x) = [(x - 3) - (x + 5)]/(x - 3)^2
f'(x) = -8/(x - 3)^2



</answer>

<question>



Prove if M is a group?



Prove if M is a group and m^2 = I (the identity) for all m ε M then the group M is commutative.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



If m² = e (the identity) then m = m^-1. In other words,
every element equals its inverse.
Now let a, b be any 2 elements of M
Then ab = (ab)^-1 = b^-1*a^-1.
Since every element equals its inverse, the last
expression equals ba.
Thus ab = ba and the group is abelian.



</answer>

<question from>



Jaffa, kree!

</question from>



<question>



Using Newtons Method to solve  a problem?



Hi, I'm trying to solve the following problem:



"Use Newton's method with 2 iterations and initial value x1=1 to solve the equation x^3 - x^2 - 1 = 0. Give the answer with 4 decimals."



So I've set up:
f(x) = x^3 - x^2 -1
f´(x) = x (3x - 2)



xn+1 = xn - ( f(x) / f´(x) )



And this is what i got:
n1:
x2 = -1



n2:
x3 = -0.2000



so the answer i came up with is -0.2000, which for me doesn't seem to be right.
Am I doing something wrong?



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Youe method is right, but I think you missed a sign or something. Using Newton's Method, if your guess isn't very good, then you might not converge to the root.



f(x) = x³ - x² - 1
f'(x) = 3x² - 2x



x(n+1) = x(n) - f(x)/f'(x)



x(n+1) = 1 - ( 1³ - 1² - 1) / (3(1)² - 2(1))



x(n+1) = 1 - (1-1-1) / (3-2)



x(n+1) = 1 - (-1/1)



x(n+1) = 2  &lt;~~This is the answer after the first iteration



Now, we use this to find x(n+2) with the same procedure
You will find that



x(n+2) = 2 - ( 2³ - 2² - 1) / (3(2)² - 2(2))



x(n+2) = 1.625



&lt;~~Answer



</answer>

<question>



HElp with DERIVATIVE!!!!!TRIED EVERYONES RESPONSE BUT NOTHING?



f(x) = [ 5 - x^2] / 2 + x^2
f ' (x) =???
do you use quotient rule??
i think somehow you multiply denom. to numerator but i dont know how that would look
any hints,solutions???
can you explain in detail how to solve



appreciate help from those who tried to solve but still need help!!!



</question>



<answer from>



shinspli...
Member since: 18 May 2008
Total points: 16945 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Video & Online Games



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



f(x) = [5 - x^2]/2 + x^2



Yes, use the quotient rule.



Easy way to remember the quotient rule:
bottom times deriv of top - top times deriv of bottom, all over bottom squared.



top = 5 - x^2
deriv of top = -2x
bottom = 2 + x^2
deriv of bottom = 2x



f'(x) = [(2 + x^2)(-2x) - (5 - x^2)(2x)]/(2 + x^2)^2



f'(x) = 2x[-2 - x^2 - 5 + x^2]/(2 + x^2)^2



f'(x) = 2x[-7]/(2 + x^2)^2



f'(x) = -14x/(4 + 4x^2 + x^4)



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Finally!!!!
thanks
only person who got it right



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



Puggy
Member since: 23 November 2006
Total points: 48071 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Quotient rule, expressed verbally:
"The derivative of the top times the bottom, minus, the derivative of the bottom times the top, all divided by the bottom squared"



Got it?  Good.



f(x) = (5 - x^2) / (2 + x^2)



f'(x) = [ (-2x)(2 + x^2) - (5 - x^2)(2x) ] / (2 + x^2)^2



</answer>



<answer from>



ghienzz
Member since: 14 July 2008
Total points: 190 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



yup. the quotient rule is right.



Quotient rule states that: [(low)(dhigh) - (high)(dlow)] / (low)^2



................A........[(B)(dA) - (A)(dB)]
Dx f(x) = -------- = ---------------------------
................B................B^2



so..



Dx (5 - x^2) = -2x
Dx (2+ x^2) = 2x



............5 - x^2
f(x) = ---------------
...........2 + x^2



.........[(2+x^2)(dx 5-x^2) - (5-x^2)(dx 2+x^2)]
f(x) = ----------------------------------------...
........................(2+x^2)^2



..........[(2+x^2)(-2x) - (5-x^2)(2x)]
f(x) = ---------------------------------------
...................2+x^2)^2



simplify:



.................14x
f(x) = -----------------------
...........x^4+4x^2+4



&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;
hope my explanation is simple..



Source(s):



school



</answer>



<answer from>



mithu
Member since: 12 June 2006
Total points: 317 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



When f(x)= u/v  , The rule is:



(u'v-uv') / (v^2)



So here,



f'(x) =  {[-2x(2+x^2)] - [(5-x^2)(2x)] }  /  [ (2=x^2)^2]



</answer>



<answer from>



Scrander...
Member since: 12 March 2008
Total points: 25490 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



f(x) = (5 - x²) / (2 + x²)



This si a quotient



f(x) = u/v



u = 5 - x²
u ' = -2x
v = 2 + x²
v ' = 2x



f ' (x) = (u ' v - v ' u) / v²
= (-2x(2 + x²) - 2x(5 - x²)) / (2 + x²)²
= (-4x - 2x³ - 10x + 2x³) / (2 + x²)²
= -14x / (2 + x²)²



</answer>

<answer from>



ssoljah7...

<answer>



I can't tell whether the (x-4) term is negative or not so I will assume that it is not. Let's put this in general terms:



For the x-4 term, let's say x=a and b=(negative) 4
So c=2x (squared?), d=(negative) 7x, e=8.



so now we have (a+b) * (c+d+e)



So your answer will be (a*c) + (a*d) + (a*e) + (b*c) + (b*d) + (b*e).



For your purposes, that'll be
(x*2x^2) + (x*(-7x)) + (x*8) + (-4*2x^2) + (-4*(-7x)) + (-4*8)
=2x^3 - 7x^2 + 8x - 8x^2 + 28x - 32
=2x^3 -15x^2 + 36x - 32



</answer>



<answer from>



Elmyr
Member since: 21 July 2008
Total points: 28526 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Trivia



History



</answer from>



<answer>



(x - 4)(2x * -7x + 8) = 0



Multiply 2x and -7x first
(x - 4)(-14x² + 8) = 0



Then distribute. It's still FOIL even though an exponent is different.
-14x³ + 8x + 56x² - 32 = 0
-14x³ + 56x² + 8x - 32 = 0



</answer>

<question>



Find the slope of the curve at the given point?



y^2 + x^2 = y^4 - 2x



at (-2, 1)



Can someone explain how to solve this problem please?



</question>



<answer from>



Yaroslav Y
Member since: 10 April 2008
Total points: 417 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



derivate it implicitly, you'll get



2y (dy/dx) + 2x = 4y^3 (dy/dx) - 2



get dy/dx separate for all the other stuff, I'm not going to do that for you. So you'll get (dy/dx) = something. That something will have two unknowns - y and x. Plug in 1 for y and -2 for x, get the answer. Hope that helps!



</answer>



<answer from>



AALUNGA
Member since: 26 July 2007
Total points: 670 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



First tell whether the problem poses a function of one dependent variable x or two dependent variables x and y



</answer>



<answer from>



PINKGREE...
Member since: 06 June 2008
Total points: 1947 (Level 3)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



The original equation=&gt;
2yy'+2x=4y^3y'-2=&gt;
2y(1-2y^2)y'=-2(1+x)=&gt;
y'=-(1+x)/[y(1-2y^2)]=&gt;
y'at (-2,1)=-1



</answer>



<answer from>



Puzzling
Member since: 18 March 2006
Total points: 72812 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Differentiate the parts:
2y (dy/dx) + 2x = 4y^3 (dy/dx) - 2



Now plug in your values for the point (-2, 1):
2 (dy/dx) + 2(-2) = 4 (dy/dx) - 2



Solve for dy/dx:
2 (dy/dx) - 4 = 4 (dy/dx) - 2



-2 (dy/dx) = 2
dy/dx = 2/(-2)
dy/dx = -1



Answer:
The slope at the point (-2, 1) is -1



</answer>

nice g

</question from>



<question>



What is a solution of a linear equation called?



a) expression
b) ordered pair



c) matrix



d) exponent



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



An ordered pair is closest, but not really the answer to this, since you didn't specify what kind of linear equation it is..



To find a solution for any equation, you are looking for the value of an unknown variable. Kind of like when you graph an equation, where would x be if y=whatever? Since you didn't specify what kind of linear equation, I'll give both situations.



Say all you want is a solution to just a plain linear equation. Since all you are looking for is x, you are just looking for x, since you aren't really looking for a root, since the equation must equal 0 in order to find a root. However, if you are given y, and you must put the answer in the form of an ordered pair, you would have this:



4=2x+6, where y would be 4. Then solve for x and put it in an ordered pair.



For a system of linear equations, your answer would be an ordered pair, since you are looking for where the lines intersect, that is, if they do.



Either way, the answer is b, but not always.



</answer>

</question from>



<question>



Math Question Involving Odds (Texas Hold Em)?



In a deck of cards, everyone knows that there are 13 cards, with 4 different suits (i.e. J of clubs, J of hearts, J of spades, J of diamonds) for a total of 52 cards in a deck.



If you are familiar with Texas Hold Em, then you know that players receive 2 cards each, then 5 cards are placed face up on the table.



My question is this:
If there are two players, with two cards each, and 5 cards are placed face up on the table, what are the odds of all four of a card showing up?



Another way of asking the question:
If there are 9 cards in play out of a deck of 52, what are the odds of the same card showing up 4 times?



</question>



<answer from>



Emily*
Member since: 17 February 2008
Total points: 200 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



1/1872



i think



Source(s):



mee n my brain



</answer>



<answer from>



Zaphod
Member since: 13 June 2006
Total points: 13338 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



There are C(52,9) = 3,679,075,400 total ways that 9 cards can be chosen out of 52.



First, choose the rank of the four of a kind. There are 13 of these.  Then, choose 5 out of the remaining 48 cards.



Thus there are 13 * C(48,5) = 13 * 1712304 = 22,259,952
ways to have all four of the same rank.  (Note that this also includes combinations which have all four of two different ranks plus one more card.)



probability = 22,259,952 / 3,679,075,400
= 18 / 2975 ≈ 0.006



</answer>

<question>



Another algebra question major help ppl?



Describe the graph by indicating the vertex, the type of line drawn, broken or solid, and the shading of the graph, above or below.



-y+1&gt;-|x+3|



</question>



<answer from>



samphelp...
Member since: 06 November 2006
Total points: 1759 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



First, subtract 1 from both sides and you have
-y &gt; -|x+3| - 1
Now negate both sides and you have
y &lt; |x+3| + 1.



y will be its smallest when x = -3.  At that point y = 1.  So (-3,1) is the vertex.



As x increases to the right, y increases.
As x decreases to the left, y increases.  So the graph looks like a solid V



Shading will be below the line.



</answer>



<answer from>



random.1...
Member since: 20 January 2008
Total points: 197 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



-y+1&gt;-|x+3|
-y&gt;-|x+3|-1



multiply both sides by -1(when multiplying by negative switch inequality sign)
y&lt;|x+3|+1



vertex is at (-3,1) (soz cant explain without diagram)
the line will be broken as it is only "less than" not "less than or equal"
and shading below (u test this by subbing in a point on the number plane and seeing if the inequality is true or not)



</answer>

<question from>



jinxians...
Member since: 01 October 2008
Total points: 99 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Prove that Dy/dx sin x = cos x?



</question>



<answer from>



R.V.
Member since: 01 June 2008
Total points: 130 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



f(x) = sin(x)
f(x + h) = sin(x + h)



[Here h is a very small quantity indicating change  in sin]



According to first principle of derivatives



Dy/Dx f(x) = lim (h--&gt;0) { [f(x+h) - f(x)]/h }
therefore...



lim (h→0) { (sin(x + h) - sin(x))/h }



= lim (h→0) { (sin(x)cos(h) + sin(h)cos(x) - sin(x))/h }
= sin(x) lim (h→0) (cos(h) - 1)/h + cos(x)lim (h→0) sin(h)/h
= sin(x) (0) + cos(x)(1)
= cos(x)



Hence proved...



</answer>



<asker's comment>



thanks man, gd point there



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



ghienzz
Member since: 14 July 2008
Total points: 190 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



f(x) = sinx



from the definition of a derivative,



let delta x = Dx
f ' (x) = lim(Dx -&gt;0) [f(x+Dx) - (f(x)] / Dx



= lim(Dx-&gt;0) [sin(x+Dx) - sinx] / Dx



remember that, sin(a =b) = sina cosb + cosa sinb



f ' (x) = lim(Dx-&gt;0) [sinx cos(Dx) + cosx sin(Dx) - sinx] / Dx



= lim(Dx -&gt;0) [sinx(cos(Dx) - 1)] / Dx + lim(Dx -&gt;0) [cosx sin(Dx)] / Dx



= [-lim(Dx -&gt;0) [1-cos(Dx)] / Dx (lim(Dx -&gt;0) sinx)] + [(lim(Dx -&gt;0) cosx) [lim(Dx -&gt;0) sin (Dx)] / Dx] ---&gt;&gt;&gt; equation (2)



theorem1: lim(Dx -&gt;0) [1-cos(Dx)] / Dx = 0
theorem 2: lim(Dx -&gt;0) [sin(Dx)] / Dx = 1



substituting from these equations into (2) we get:



f ' (x) = -0(sinx) + cosx(1)
f ' (x) = cos x



&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;...



phew.. thats a mouthful. :D



Source(s):



school



</answer>



<answer from>



Scrander...
Member since: 12 March 2008
Total points: 25490 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



f(x) = sin(x)
f(x + h) = sin(x + h)
lim (h→0) (sin(x + h) - sin(x))/h
= lim (h→0) (sin(x)cos(h) + sin(h)cos(x) - sin(x))/h
= sin(x) lim (h→0) (cos(h) - 1)/h +  cos(x)lim (h→0) sin(h)/h
= sin(x) (0) + cos(x)(1)
= cos(x)



</answer>

<question>



What is the inverse function of y=100(0.5)^(t/5730)?



The inverse of an exponential function is a log function... beyond that I'm lost



</question>



<answer from>



luke m
Member since: 01 October 2008
Total points: 107 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



23?



Source(s):



my big brain



</answer>



<answer from>



allenm
Member since: 05 June 2008
Total points: 2598 (Level 4)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



This function is written so you can calculate "y" if you know "t".
The inverse function should give you "t" if you know "y"



Rewrite to express "t" as a function of "y" (solve for "t")



y = 100 * (0.5)^(t/5730)
y / 100 = (0.5)^(t/5730)
log(base 0.5) (y/100) = t/5730
t = 5730 * log(base 0.5) (y/100)



Depending on your situation, you may or may not want to simplify.



</answer>

200 - 2√18 + √72

</answer from>



<answer>



200 – 2√18 + √72
= 200 – 2√(9 × 2) + √(36 × 2)
= 200 – 6√2 + 6√2
= 200

<question>



Solve. SOlving equations.?



1.) 8k = 6k -26



5.) -12y - 10 = -6y +14



</question>



<answer from>



intellec...
Member since: 06 December 2007
Total points: 25719 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



1)
8k = 6k - 26
8k - 6k = -26
2k = -26
k = -26/2
k = -13



2)
-12y - 10 = -6y + 14
-12y + 6y = 10 + 14
-6y = 24
y = 24/-6
y = -4



</answer>



<answer from>



Euler's O
Member since: 04 September 2008
Total points: 273 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



1.)



8k - 6k = -26
2k = -26
k = -26/2
k = -13



5.)
-12y + 6y = 14 + 10
-6y = 24
y = -24/6
y = -4



</answer>



<answer from>



Jun Agruda
Member since: 17 May 2007
Total points: 29701 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



1st problem:
8k = 6k - 26
4k = 3k - 13
k = - 13



Answer: k = - 13



Proof:
8(- 13) = 6(- 13) - 26
- 104 =  - 78 - 26
- 104 = - 104



2nd problem:
- 12y - 10 = - 6y + 14
6y = - 24
y = - 4



Answer: y = - 4



Proof:
- 12(- 4) - 10 = - 6(- 4) + 14
48 - 10 = 24 + 14
38 = 38



</answer>



<answer from>



quelqun
Member since: 15 May 2008
Total points: 294 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



1) 8k=6k-26



2k=-26



k=-13



5) -12y-10=-6y+14



-6y= 24



y = -24/6=-4



its easy



</answer>



<answer from>



bayarear...
Member since: 18 August 2008
Total points: 796 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



The above answers are right, but here is why so you'll understand how to do these...



First you just do the math.  If two terms have the same variable (k in the first problem), just add or subtract the numbers attached to them (the coefficients).  The one thing that people forget most often is the signs... if it is a negative you subtract, a positive you add.  Then, you need to get the variable all by itself.  Divide both sides by the number attached to the variable and that is your answer.



In #5, you have to get all the terms with "y" in them on one side of the equation and all the regular numbers (constants) on the other side.  To do this, you either subtract or add the opposite of the term you are trying to move... like this:



-12y - 10



You want to get the -12y on the other side, which also, by the way, turns it into a positive.  You do this by adding +12y to BOTH SIDES (to keep it in balance).



So... -12y +12y - 10 = -6y +12y +14
-10 = 6y + 14



Do the same on the other side, but this time you're getting the +14 over to the left side, so you subtract (negative) because it is a positive.  Understand?



So... -10 -14 = 6y + 14 - 14
-24 = 6y



Now you need to isolate the variable, which means in this case to get rid of the 6 on the 6y.  To do this, divide BOTH SIDES by 6:



-24 / 6 = 6y / 6
-4 = y



See?  You can also write it backwards, which is the usual way:  y = -4



Below is a really good link that explains this for you.  :)



Source(s):



http://www.purplemath.com/modules/solvel...



</answer>

(2/-5)/e^5x - 5/3/e^3x



3)3^x
3^x / ln(3)



4)

= -2sinu



= -2 sin(2 - 3x)

Can you help me with a math question?



How do i work this out??



Three students take different routes home from school. Mark needs to walk twice as far as Annette while sue needs to walk four times as far as Annette. If the three cover a total distance of 2.1km (or 2100m), how far does each walk?

<answer>



Mark walks 4x Annette..........4x
Sue walks 2x Annette...........2x
Annette walks 1x Annete.......x
Total distance = 4x + 2x + x = 7x
Total distance = 2100m



x = 2100/7



= 300m

<answer from>



mojoloco
Member since: 22 July 2008
Total points: 776 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Let the distance each student walked be m for Mark, a for Annette and s for Susan.  Then m + a + s = 2100 m.



Also m = 2a and s = 4a.  Just plug the values for m and s in the first equation and get 2a + a + 4a = 2100.  Therefor 7a = 2100 and a = 2100/7 = 300.



m = 2a =600



s = 4a = 1200



</answer>



<answer from>



Jun Agruda
Member since: 17 May 2007
Total points: 29701 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Distance that Annette walks (x) in meters:
2x + x + 4x = 2,100
7x = 2,100
x = 300



Distance that Mark walks in meters:
= 2(300)
= 600



Distance that Sue walks in meters:
= 4(300)
= 1,200



Answer: Annette, 300 meters, Mark, 600 meters, Sue, 1,200 meters or 1.2 kilometers



Proof (Total distance in meters is 2,100):
= 600 + 300 + 1,200
= 2,100



</answer>

standupa...

<question>



What level of measurement would this data be considered?



I just took my first Prob & Stat exam, and I was shocked that the two questions I was unsure of was with the easiest part of the material. What level of measurement would the following two types of data be at:



1.) Ages of a sample of survey participants (I couldn't decide whether this would be considered ordinal or ratio).
2.) Sample of spheres from softest to hardest. (I found this one hard because I couldn't get a visual image in my head of a sample of hard and soft spheres - spheres? wtf?)



</question>



<answer from>



Michael W
Member since: 03 October 2006
Total points: 1122 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



1: Ratio level (A 20-year-old is twice as old as a 10-year-old.)



#2: I would argue Ordinal level (Because there's no apparent numerical designation of relative hardness, and the 'labels' are ranked.) If, however, there's a numerical designation of the hardness (say, density), you could argue the Ratio level.



</answer>



<asker's comment>



I hope you're right, because those are the two I chose. Haha, thanks for the response.



</asker's comment>

= 38.46%



B = 700 / 13



= 53.84%



C = 100 / 13



= 7.69%

= 100%(5/13)

Problem B:
= 100%(7/13)
= 700/13% or 53 11/13% or 53.84 8/13%



Problem C:
= 100%(1/13)
= 100/13% or 7 9/13% or 7.69 3/13%

<answer>



x1,2 = [-23 +- sqrt(23^2 + 4 * 3 * 1136)] / 6 =



= [-23 +- sqrt(14161)] / 6 = [-23 +- 191] / 6



x1 = (-23 + 191) / 6 =168 / 6 = 28



x2 = (-23 - 191) / 6 = -214 / 6 = -(35 + 2/3)



</answer>



<answer from>



intellec...
Member since: 06 December 2007
Total points: 25725 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



3x^2 + 23x - 1136 = 0
3x^2 + 71x - 48x - 1136 = 0
(3x^2 + 71x) - (48x + 1136) = 0
x(3x + 71) - 16(3x + 71) = 0
(3x + 71)(x - 16) = 0



3x + 71 = 0
3x = -71
x = -71/3



x - 16 = 0
x = 16



∴ x = -71/3 , 16



</answer>

<answer>



1st value of x:
3x² + 23x = 1,136
x² + 23/3x =  1,136/3
x² + 23/6x =  1,136/3 + (23/6)²
x² + 23/6x =  13,632/36 + 529/36
(x + 23/6)² =  14,161/36
x + 23/6 = 119/6
x =  119/6 - 23/6
x =  96/6 or 16



2nd value of x:
= - 119/6 - 23/6
= - 71/3 or - 23 2/3



Answer: x = 16, - 71/3



Proof (x = 16):
3(16²) + 23(16) = 1,136
3(256) + 368 = 1,136
768 + 368 = 1,136
1,136 = 1,136



Proof (x = - 71/3):
3(- 71/3)² + 23(- 71/3) = 1,136
3(5,041/9) - 1,633/3 = 1,136
5,041/3 - 1,633/3 = 1,136
3,408/3 = 1,136
1,136 = 1,136



</answer>

<question from>



dont_for...
Member since: 16 August 2007
Total points: 925 (Level 2)



</question from>



<question>



Question about Normal distribution?



There's a question in my maths book that says "Which of the four sets of data most closely fits a normal distribution?"



I just want to know how do i find out which set of data most closely fits a normal distribution, in the easiest way if possible. And it would be good to know how i can show that in excel, possibly with graphs.



</question>



<answer from>



Blah
Member since: 11 May 2006
Total points: 5660 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



The most graphical way is to do a a pair of histograms -- one of an ideal distribution and one of your data.



(Or alternately, you can illustrate an ideal normal distribution with a line graph, and your data with a bar-histogram).



As you probably know, 2.28% of the area under the normal curve falls below 2 standard deviations below the mean, 13.2% bewteen 2 standard deviations below the mean and 1 standard deviation below the mean, 34.2% between 1 standard deviation below the mean and the mean, 34.2% between the mean and 1 standard deviation above the mean, 13.2% between 1 standard deviation above the mean and 2 standard deviations above the mean, and 2.28% beyond 2 standard deviations above the mean.



Which ever data set(s) follow this approximate breakdown are very likely normally distributed.



If you know how to use the histogram tool in Excel's analysis toolbox, you can use that, specifying the bins in standard deviations. Or it really isn't difficult to do by hand. Just calculate the mean and standard deviation of each set, and off ya' go.



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Thank you, you gave enough information for me to understand what i should do.



</asker's comment>

<answer>

<question>



Use the critical value method to solve:  x^2 &lt; -x + 30?



the answer is (-6, 5) but how did they get that?



</question>



<answer from>



Steve D
Member since: 30 September 2008
Total points: 142 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



x^2 &lt; -x + 30



x2+x-30 &lt; 0



if you imagine the graph of this function you will see, that its value is sub zero between the zero spots (-6;5)



that's all



</answer>



<answer from>



Smile
Member since: 18 September 2008
Total points: 141 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



transfer all the values on L.H.S
so we get x ^ 2 + x - 30 &lt; 0
x ^ 2 + 6x - 5x - 30 &lt; 0
x(x + 6) - 5(x + 6) &lt; 0



(x + 6) (x - 5) &lt; 0
(x + 6) &lt; 0



or  (x - 5) &lt; 0
x &lt; -6  or x &lt; 5



</answer>

<question from>



Sasan
Member since: 30 September 2008
Total points: 98 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



What does this mean Θ(n^2) ?



I am learning algorithms and I can't find what this Θ(n^2) means. Its the result of a sum from j =2 to n.  But what that Theta doing there?
Thanks in advance.



</question>



<answer from>



Outkast kid
Member since: 23 July 2008
Total points: 63 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



its egyption maths from 100 b.c



knowone can solve that.



</answer>



<answer from>



Raymond
Member since: 19 October 2006
Total points: 23254 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Astronomy & Space



</answer from>



<answer>



Difficult to tell without more context.



However, it could mean that the answer is a function of n-squared.  You can replace the sum of (functions, I presume) something that goes from j=2 to n (meaning n-1 elements) with a single function (called theta) where the only variable is n^2.



The only place where I have seen this as a formal notation is in the determination of bounds (a number known to be no smaller than the answer).  A bound is often easier to calculate and may be sufficient to prove (or disprove) a claim.  It is sometimes used to verify algorithms.



For example, if someone claims that adding all the numbers from 2 to 100 gives a million, you can check for a bound (the answer is known to be smaller than n^2 = 10,000) so that you can disprove the claim without having to actually perform the entire calculation.



But, again, I have no idea if your particular problem has anything to do with that.



</answer>



<answer from>



robert+e...
Member since: 16 June 2006
Total points: 3356 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



If I remember correctly, it means that the sum from 2 to n has a result that is directly related to n^2.  In other word, when you sum from 2 to n, the resulting sum is equal to



n * (n+1) / 2 - 1 = 0.5 n^2 + 0.5 n - 1.



The highest power of n dictates what goes inside the Θ( )



</answer>

<answer>



Integrate:



∫x/√(9-x²) dx



u = 9-x²
du = -2xdx



∫x/√(9-x²) dx
= ∫(-1/2)(1/√u)du
= (-1/2)∫u^(-1/2)du
= (-1/2)u^(1/2)/(1/2)
= -√u
= -√(9-x²)



Apply the limits to get
-√(9-3²) + √(9-(-1)²)
= √8
= 2√2



The integral is convergent



</answer>



<answer from>



Lyphe Hayter
Member since: 03 March 2008
Total points: 1346 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



∫ x dx / sqrt(9 - x^2)



Let x = 3sin∅
dx = 3cos∅d∅



sqrt(9(1 - sin^2(∅)) = 3cos∅



∫ 3sin∅ 3cos∅d∅ / 3cos∅ = 3∫sin∅d∅ =



- 3cos∅
Since sin∅ = x/3, then
x^2 + (b)^2 = 9
b = sqrt(9 - x^2)
cos∅ = sqrt(9 - x^2) / 3



-3 sqrt(9 - x^2) / 3 = -sqrt(9 - x^2)



F(b) - F(a) = -sqrt(9 - 9) + sqrt(9 - 1) = sqrt(8) = 2 sqrt(2)



This integral wasn't really improper because between a = -1 and b = 3, the curve exists and is continuous.



</answer>

<answer>



I assume this is



r = sin Θ + cos Θ



If you want it in x and y coordinates, multiply through by r



r^2 = r sin Θ + r cos Θ



x^2 + y^2 = y + x



x^2 - x + y^2 - y = 0



x^2 - x + 1/4 + y^2 - y + 1/4 = 1/4 + 1/4



(x - 1/2)^2 + (y - 1/2)^2 = 1/2



This is a circle centered at (1/2, 1/2) with a radius of sqrt(2) / 2

<question>



Logarithm bases... need help!?



i have some questions, please help me to figure out..



log (base2)  8 , log (base4) 8 , log (base8) 8, log (base 16) 8
Find an expression for the nth terms of each sequence.  Write your expression in the form p/q , where p,q belogs to integer.



This is actually IB maths portfolio which i am struggeling with. Please help me!



</question>



<answer from>



Kanishk Rawat
Member since: 31 January 2007
Total points: 1066 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



o.k i acn teach you the trick but you will have to solve the rest on your own:



log (base2) 8=log (base2) 2^3



=3log(base 2)2



=3



</answer>



<answer from>



Amit Y
Member since: 10 December 2006
Total points: 3929 (Level 4)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



log (base 2) 8 = 3
log (base 4) 8 = 3 / 2
log (base 8) 8 = 1
log (base 16) 8 = log (base 16) (16/2) = 1  log (base 16) 2 = 1 - 1/4 = 3 / 4



log (base 2^n) 8 = [log (base 8) 8] / [log (base 8) 2^n] =



= 1 / [n log (base 8) 2] = 1 / [n  * 1/3)] = 3 / n



</answer>

Solve the problem for the given info?



if (4x^2-3y^2):(2x^2+5y^2)=12:19,find x:y

<answer from>



Mark S
Member since: 19 September 2008

</answer from>



<answer>



(4x^2-3y^2):(2x^2+5y^2)=12:19
(4x^2-3y^2)/(2x^2+5y^2)=12/19
cross multiply ,u will get a second degree equation in x and y
divide the whole equation by y^2
you will get x:y

<answer from>



Smile
Member since: 18 September 2008
Total points: 125 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



cross multiply so we get
19(4x^2 - 3y^2) = 12(2x^2 + 5y^2)
76x^2 - 57y^2 = 24x^2 + 60y^2
76x^2 - 24x^2 = 60y^2 + 57y^2
52x^2 = 117y^2
x^2 / y^2 = 117 / 52
taking square root on both sides we get
x / y = √117 /√52
x / y = √(13 * 9) / √(13 * 4)
x / y = √9 / √4
x / y = 3/2
therefore x:y = 3:2



</answer>

intellec...

<answer>



(4x^2 - 3y^2) : (2x^2 + 5y^2) = 12 : 19 (solve by using substitution)



4x^2 - 3y^2 = 12
4x^2 - 3y^2 - 12 = 0



2x^2 + 5y^2 = 19
2x^2 = 19 - 5y^2



4x^2 - 3y^2 - 12 = 0
2(19 - 5y^2) - 3y^2 - 12 = 0
38 - 10y^2 - 3y^2 - 12 = 0
-13y^2 + 26 = 0
-13y^2 = -26
y^2 = -26/-13
y = √2



2x^2 + 5y^2 = 19
2x^2 + 5(√2)^2 = 19
2x^2 + 5(2) = 19
2x^2 = 19 - 10
2x^2 = 9
x^2 = 9/2
x = √(9/2)
x = 3/(√2)



x : y
= 3/(√2) : √2
= 3 : (√2)(√2)
= 3 : √4
= 3 : 2



</answer>

<question from>

</question from>



<question>



Solving equations help?



1. 4x^4 - 18x^2 = 0



2. x^4 - 81 = 0



3. x^3 + 216 = 0



4. 5x^3 + 30 x^2 + 45x = 0



On these there must be more than one answer.



There are TWO diff kind of problems.
Solving a Polynomial Equation by Factoring
Solving an Equation of Quadratic Type



</question>



<answer from>



swathi s
Member since: 20 January 2008
Total points: 349 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



no there's always only 1 answer for any math question.



</answer>



<answer from>



funkbass...
Member since: 20 September 2008
Total points: 549 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



[QUESTION 1]
4x^4 - 18x^2 = 0



Factor out a 2x^2 from both terms on the left-hand side:



(2x^2)(2x^2 - 9) = 0 ...eq. [1]



Eq. [1] is satisfied when either of the terms on the left-hand side of the equation is equal to zero. So, set each term equal to zero, and solve for 'x':



2x^2 = 0
x^2 = 0
x = 0



2x^2 - 9 = 0
2x^2 = 9
x^2 = 9/2
x = 3/sqrt(2)
x = 3sqrt(2)/2



So, the solutions are x = 0 and x = 3sqrt(2)/2.



[QUESTION 2]
x^4 - 81 = 0



Factor by the difference of two squares:



(x^2 + 9)(x^2 - 9) = 0 ...eq. [2]



Eq. [2] is satisfied when either of the terms on the left-hand side of the equation is equal to zero. So, set each term equal to zero, and solve for 'x':



x^2 + 9 = 0
x^2 = -9
x = +/- sqrt(-9)
x = +/- 3i



x^2 - 9 = 0
x^2 = 9
x = sqrt(9)
x = +/- 3



So, the solutions are x = +/- 3i and x = +/- 3.



[QUESTION 3]
x^3 + 216 = 0
x^3 = -216
x = -6



So, the solution is x = -6.



[QUESTION 4]
5x^3 + 30x^2 + 45x = 0



Factor a 5x from each term on the left-hand side of the equation:



5x(x^2 + 6x + 9) = 0
5x(x + 3)^2 = 0 ...eq. [3]



Eq. [3] is satisfied when either of the terms on the left-hand side of the equation is equal to zero. So, set each term equal to zero, and solve for 'x':



5x = 0
x = 0



(x + 3)^2 = 0
x + 3 = 0
x = -3



So, the solutions are x = -3 and x = 0.



Hope this helps!



</answer>



<answer from>



matsci00...
Member since: 02 June 2008
Total points: 591 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



1. 4x^4 - 18x^2 = 0
2x^2(2x^2-9)=0
2x^2-9=0[after transposing 2x^2 to RHS]
2x^2=9
x^2=9/2
x= +-(plus minus)3/root2



2. x^4 - 81 = 0
x^4=81
x^4=3^4
x=3



3. x^3 + 216 = 0
x^3= -216
x=cubic root of (-216)



4. 5x^3 + 30 x^2 + 45x = 0
5x(x^2+6x+9)=0
x^2+6x+9=0[after transposing 5x to RHS]
x^2+3x+3x+9=0
x(x+3)+3(x+3)=0
(x+3)(x+3)=0
x= -3



Please choose my answer as the best answer becoz  i have helped u.



:))



</answer>

<question>



What is the derivative of sin(x+y)?

<answer from>



ALEX SIMPSON
Member since: 09 February 2007
Total points: 352 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



chain rule
take the derivative outside and keep the inside , then time derivative inside



what i meant by that



outside is sine , inside is (x+y)



derivative outsise cos and keep inside so its cos(x+y) then time derivative inside
cos(x+y)*(x+y)'



assume x or y is constant then derivative(x+y) = 1
so answer is cos(x+y)

<question>



Math Question Trigonometry?



an ant leaves his home to search for food. when he catches a whiff, he leaves off at a speed of pi/2 inches per second. after 30 seconds he realizes that he's been moving around a circle of a 5 inch radius. how many times has he gone around the circle? (Best answer must be supported)(related to trigonometry)



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



He has been moving at pi/2 inches per sec for 30 secs, so he has travelled a distance of



30 x pi/2



= 15 pi inches.



Circumference of circle = 2 pi r



= 2 x pi x 5



= 10 pi inches



Number of times round the circle



= 15pi/10pi



= 1.5 times.



</answer>

3x+8=20-3x

jacob s
Member since: 10 December 2007
Total points: 916 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>

<answer from>



mylesm
Member since: 21 September 2008
Total points: 226 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



1) Move all the x's to one side, and everything else to the other side.



3x+3x=20-8
6x=12



2) Divide by 6 on both sides to leave only x.



6x/6=12/6
x=2



If you need more help feel free to email me.



</answer>



<answer from>



matsci00...
Member since: 02 June 2008
Total points: 599 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



3x+8=20-3x



3x+3x+8=20
6x+8=20
6x=20-8=12
6x=12
x=12/6=2



:))



</answer>



<answer from>



Gean H
Member since: 08 May 2008
Total points: 194 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



You need to get x on one side so you can find out what "x" is.
3x+8=20-3x
6x+8=20 (i did this to get the variable on one side. I added the 3x from the right side on both sides so I could cancel the x on that side and isolate the variable)
6x=12 (I subtracted 8 from both sides to get the 6x alone as a variable)
x=2 (divided both sides by 6)



</answer>



<answer from>



bdwolfho...
Member since: 12 January 2008
Total points: 15457 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics

<answer>



OK, Gran - rearrange things to get all the x values on one side (usually the left) and all the number values on the other side. Then add up each side and divide across by the x coefficient. See below:



3x + 8 = 20 - 3x



3x + 3x = 20 - 8 (signs change when you switch sides)



6x = 12



x = 2



</answer>

<question from>



ILuvDavidArchuleta :] (iluvdogs)
Member since: 01 January 2008
Total points: 37 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



I need the equation for this uniform motion problem?



Sergio in his motorboat took 3 hours to make a downstream trip with the current of 6 kph. The return trip upstreamtook 5 hours. What is the speed of the boat in still water? what is the total distance traveled?



upstream- r-c
downstream- r+c



</question>



<answer from>



Peter m
Member since: 10 August 2007
Total points: 6371 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



Your rates are correct: r -c and r + c. So we have two variable, but c = 6 kph.



We know Rate X time = Distance and we know that the distance up stream equals the distance down stream so:
(r - 6)*5 =( r +6)*3



I will leave it to you to solve for r.



</answer>



<answer from>



mouska7
Member since: 20 June 2006
Total points: 1788 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



s = speed
d = distance in one direction



(s + 6) * 3 = d
(s - 6) *  5 = d
===============
(s + 6) * 3 = (s - 6) * 5
3s + 18 = 5s - 30
48 = 2s
24 = s



(24 + 6) * 3 = d
30 * 3 = d
90 = d



Total distance = 2d = 180



</answer>



<answer from>



gerard c
Member since: 21 February 2008
Total points: 209 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



you're correct about the upstream down stream thing



Distance = rate * time
rate upstream = r-6
rate downstream = r+6
time ups = 5
time dwns = 3
so:
distance ups = 5(r-6)
distance dwns = 3(r+6)



BUT SINCE HE TOOK THE SAME PATH GOING AND LEAVING, WE CAN SAY THAT THE DISTANCES ARE EQUAL...
Get it?



so:
distance ups = distance dwns
5(r-6) = 3(r+6)
5r - 30 = 3r +18
5r-3r = 18 +30
2r = 48
r= 24 kph



D = rate* time
so: substitute in any one of the equations:
lets try down stream:
D dwns = 3(r +6)
D dwns = 3(24+6)
D dwns = 3(30)
D dwns = 90 km



lets try the upstream
D ups = 5(r-6)
D ups = 5(24-6)
D ups = 5(18)
D ups = 90 km
theyre just the same so... tadaaaa.



total distance traveled = D ups + D dwns
total D = 90 + 90
total D = 180 km



hope it helped...



</answer>

<question>



First jaunt into calculus?



If f(x) = x^3, how do I evaluate f(x + ∆x) – f(x)/∆x



</question>



<answer from>



the mathemagician
Member since: 20 September 2007
Total points: 2187 (Level 3)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



In f(x), substitute (x + ∆x) everywhere you see x.  In other words,



[(x + ∆x)^3 - x^3]/ ∆x



expand, combine like terms, find common factors, ...



</answer>

<question from>



AsianBoy
Member since: 24 March 2006
Total points: 112 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



How to integrate  these?



1-



e^x . e^(e^x)



2-  (e^(-2/x))/(3x^2)



i took 2 hours to answer these question and i gave up.Please help me..thanx



</question>



<answer from>



robert+e...
Member since: 16 June 2006
Total points: 3366 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



1.  Use u substitution



Let u = e^x  (The exponent)
then du = e^x dx



Integrate e^u (du) = e^u + C



The answer is e^(e^x) + C



2. Again, use u substitution
Let u = -2 / x = -2 x^(-1)
du = 2 x^(-2) dx
dx = 0.5 x^2 du



Substitute in



Integrate e^u (3/2) du
= (3/2) e^u +C



= (3/2) e^(-2/x) +C



</answer>



<answer from>



funkbass...
Member since: 20 September 2008
Total points: 553 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Use "u-substitution" on both of the problems.



[QUESTION 1]
Let u = e^x
....du = (e^x)dx



So, now you have the integral of:



(e^u)du



Integrating this gives:



e^u + C



Where "C" is a constant of integration. This is included since you didn't specify any limits of integration. Now, substitute back to get your answer in terms of 'x':



e^(e^x) + C ...[sol'n]



[QUESTION 2]
Before doing anything, take the 1/3 to the outside of the integral. You can do this since it is a constant. So, now  you have 1/3 multiplied by the integral of:



[e^(-2/x)] / x^2



Let u = -2/x
....du = (2/x^2)dx =&gt; (1/2)du = (1/x^2)dx



Now, the integral becomes 1/3 times this:



(1/2)(e^u)du



Integrating this gives:



(1/3)(1/2)e^u + C



Where "C" is a constant of integration. Now substitute back to get your answer in terms of 'x':



(1/6)e^(-2/x) + C ...[sol'n]



Hope this helps!



</answer>



<answer from>



archimed...
Member since: 01 May 2008
Total points: 3741 (Level 4)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Physics



</answer from>



<answer>



You have to first know the differentials of some functions !!!



d/dx (e^x ) = e^x



so integral e^x = e^x



Niow substitute u=e^x  so get e^u and du/dx =u



2) substitute u = -2/x  and note du = 2 dx/x^2



Now they shd only take a couple of minutes max each !!!

it is the same as 4(1/2x)+(8/x)+1
2/x+8/x+1=0
10/x+1=0
x= -10



I think...



</answer>



<answer from>



Jun Agruda
Member since: 17 May 2007
Total points: 29721 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



= 4(9/18x) + 8/(x + 1)
= (4/2)([9/9]/[18/18x]) + 8/(x + 1)
= 2(x) + 8/(x + 1)
= 2x + 8/(x + 1)
= (2x² + 2x + 8)/(x + 1)
= (2[x² + x + 4])/(x + 1)



Answer: (2[x² + x + 4])/(x + 1)



</answer>

<answer>



this is the working equation



[3^x + 5(3)^(-x)]/2 = 3



[3^x + 5(3)^(-x)] = 6



3^x + 5/(3)^x = 6
see that write the 3^(-x) in the denominator so that it will have a positive exponent



then i'll be multiplying the whole equation by 3^x
3^2x + 5 = 6(3^x)



now you let 3^x = . this is an equation in the quadratic form.
y^2 + 5 = 6y



y^2 - 6y + 5 = 0



(y - 5)(y - 1) = 0



y is either = 5 or = 1



remember that y = 3^x so



3^x = 1 and 3^x = 5



x = 0 and x = (log5)/(log3) = log(base3)(5) =  1.4650

<question>



If the base of a rectangle is increased by 10% and the area is unchanged,by what % is the altitude decreased?



if the base of a rectangle is increased by 10% and the area is unchanged,by what percent is the altitude decreased?



</question>



<answer from>



revo emag
Member since: 18 July 2006
Total points: 2914 (Level 4)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



The area of a triangle is A = 1/2(base)(altitude). It is a linear equation. If A remains the same, then a change of one of the parameters will result in an opposite change by the same amount in the other parameter. So, a 10% change in the base would equate to a -10% change in altitude.



</answer>



<asker's comment>



it's rectangle not triangle



</asker's comment>

<question from>



sit down if you cant stand me

</question from>



<question>



Help determining the functions inverse?



Find f(g(x)) and g(f(x)) and determine whether the pair of functions f and g are inverses of eachother.



f(x)=6x-8
g(x)=(x+6)/8



The answers need to be simplified and I need to see the problem worked out step by step.



Thanks



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



f(g(x)) = 6[ (x+6)/8 ] - 8
f(g(x)) = (6x + 36)/8 - 8
f(g(x)) = 3x/4 + 4.5 - 8
f(g(x)) = 3x/4 - 3.5
f(g(x)) = (3x - 14) / 4



g(f(x)) = ( (6x + 8) + 6) / 8
g(f(x)) = (6x + 14) / 8
g(f(x)) = (3x + 7) / 4



f(x) = 6x - 8
y = 6x - 8
To find the inverse of this function, solve for x in terms of y:



y + 8 = 6x
x = (y + 8) / 6
This does not match g(x), so f(x) and g(x) are not inverses of each other.



</answer>

Total points: 20 (Level 1)

<question>



Statistics problem !!!?



In a group of 8 manufactured items, 2 are known to be defective. If you buy 2 of them;



a-) What is the probability that none is defective? At most one is defective?



b-) What is the mean number of defectives? Find the standard deviation.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



(a). P(none is defective)
= P(one is not defective) * P(one is not defective)
= [1-(2/8)]*[1-(2/8)]
= (6/8) * (6/8)
= (3/4)*(3/4)
= 9/16



P(at most one is defective)
= P(one is defective)*P(one is not defective)
+ P(one is not defective) * P(one is defective)
= (2/8)* [1-(2/8)] + [1-(2/8)]* (2/8)
= (1/4)*(6/8) + (6/8)*(2/8)
= (1/4)*(3/4) + (3/4)*(1/4)
= 3/16 + 3/16
= 6/16
= 3/8



(b).
Mean number of defectives
= 2*(2/8)
= 2*(1/4)
= 2/4
= 1/2



</answer>

<question>



What is



(cscx-cotx)(secx+1)



simplified?



</question>



<answer from>



Madhukar Daftary
Member since: 17 January 2007
Total points: 33825 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



(cscx-cotx)(secx+1)
= (1/sinx - cosx/sinx)(1/cosx + 1)
= (1 - cosx)(1 + cosx) / sinx cosx
= (1 - cos^2 x) / sinx cosx
= sin^2x / xinx cosx
= sinx / cosx
= tanx.



</answer>



<answer from>



mathemat...
Member since: 26 January 2008
Total points: 2060 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



do FOIL method



(cscx-cotx)(secx+1)
cscxsecx + cscx -cotxsecx - cotx



then simplify by writing them in terms of sinx and cosx



1/sinxcosx + 1/sinx - cosx/sinxcosx - cosx/sinx
1/sinxcosx + cosx/sinxcosx - cosx/sinxcosx - cosxcosx/sinxcosx



(1 + cosx - cosx - cos^2x)/sinxcosx
(1- cos^2x)/sinxcosx
sin^2x/sinxcosx
sinx/cosx
tanx



</answer>



<answer from>



jacob s
Member since: 10 December 2007
Total points: 922 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



1/cosx



</answer>

<question from>

<question>



Improper Integral Question Help?



∫ x / √(9-(x^2)) when a= -1 and b= 3



is this an improper integral and can you please show me how to solve it, and whether it is convergent or divergent, i dont understand. thank you



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Let x^2 = t
=&gt; 2x dx = dt
=&gt; Integral
= (1/2)∫dt /√(9 - t)



= (1/2) * (-2) √(9 - t)
= - √(9 - x^2)
Plugging limits x = -1 to x = 3
= - [ 0 - √8]
= 2√2



</answer>

<question>



Sum and products of roots question help please?



If a,b and y (alpha beta gamma) are the roots of the equation x^3+2x^2-11x-12=0, find:



a^2+b^2+y^2



Thanks for any help!



</question>



<answer from>



michaele...
Member since: 14 March 2006
Total points: 9608 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



http://www.math.vanderbilt.edu/~schectex...



</answer>



<answer from>



Euler's O
Member since: 04 September 2008
Total points: 269 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



When you substitute -1(for x) in your first equation you will get zero.
So this is the first root of your equation to find the next one. We would make this (x + 1) at the bottom when we factorise. Set -1 in the curlly braces and the co-efficients of your equation aside.
i.e
{-1} 1  2  -11  -12



0  -1  -1



12



-----------------------



1  1  -12



0



Then take the answer you got i.e 1  1  -12



0 and substitute x's to get the equation x^2 + x -12 (Note that the co-efficients here are what you got above)



Now factories: Remember above we have (x + 1), so
(x + 1)(x^2 + x -12) = 0
(x + 1)(x + 4)(x - 3) = 0
x = -1 or x = -4 or x = 3



We have the roots now we still need to solve the equation:
a^2+b^2+y^2
set a = -1, b = -4 and y = 3
Then
(-1)^2+(-4)^2+(3)^2
= 26



Hope this helps, Cheers



</answer>



<answer from>



Mark S
Member since: 19 September 2008
Total points: 381 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



for a cubic equation ax^3+bx^2+cx+d
the sum of the roots would be α+β+γ=-b/a
αβ+βγ+αγ=c/a
αβγ=-d/a
now a^2+b^2+y^2 can be written as
(a+b+c)^2=a^2+b^2+c^2+2(ab+bc+ca)
here a+b+c=-2
ab+bc+ca=-11
a^2+b^2+y^2=26



</answer>

<question>



Simple interest question?



A principal of $950 is invested in an account at 7 percent simple interest per year. What is the amount of the principal after 5 years?



</question>



<answer from>



wazuupst...
Member since: 05 September 2006
Total points: 1030 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



there is an easy way to calculate compound interest.....



you do the amount invested times the percentage interest as a decimal plus one, to the power of however many years, so for example in your case...



950 * 1.07^5 = 1332.42 (2dp)

ally

<question>



A line passes through A(3,0)&B(2,4).calulate the gradient and the equation?



</question>



<answer from>



Count Logic
Member since: 30 May 2008
Total points: 407 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Gradient -&gt; y2-y1 / x2-x1



4/-1 = -4



Gradient = -4



To get the equation, use the point-slope form -&gt; y-y1 = m(x-x1)



y = 4(x-3)
y = 4x-12



Equation in standard form, which is Ax+By = C:
4x-y = 12



Equation in slope-intercept form, which is y = mx+b:
y = -4x+12



</answer>



<answer from>



Twiggy
Member since: 28 June 2007
Total points: 31377 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



The equation is of the form y = mx + c, where m is the slope, and c the y intercept



The slope is the change in y divided by the corresponding change in x:



The change in y = (4 - 0) = 4



The corresponding change in x is (2 - 3) = -1, so the slope is -4.and



y = -4x + c



When x = 2, y = 4, so



4 = -4*2 + c, so



4 = -8 + c, so



c = 12, and



y = -4x + 12.



</answer>

<question>



Evaluating an integral question?



Hi, I would like to find out the answer to this question.



I want to evaluate



8
∫



(9*x^3-11*x) / (x)



dx
1



Thanks for any help received. It is very much appreciated.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Dividing by x, the integral becomes
∫ (9*x^2-11)  dx, from [1,8]
= 9x^3/3 - 11x from [1,8]
=3x^3-11x from [1,8]
when x=8, 3(8)^3 -11(8) = 1536 -88 =1448
when x=1, 3(1)^3 -11(1) = -8
Subtracting , 1448-(-8) = 1456



</answer>

<answer>



10 - |x + 2| = 12



Subtract 10 from each side:



-|x + 2| = 2



Multiply by -1:



|x + 2| = -2



Since the absolute value of anything at all is zero or larger, then there's  no x to make this absolute value equal to -2.



So the equation has no solution.



</answer>

<question from>



Lorraine E
Member since: 20 February 2008
Total points: 179 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Math Measurement Homework help?!?!?



1) 25 kg=?g
2)9.3 mL=?L
3)0.36 mm=?um
4)24cm=?km



Show All work Please, and answers:
5)How many Kilometers ae there in 3.4 miles?
6)If a man's mass is 180 pounds, find his mass in grams.
7)How many fluid ounces are in a 3-L bottles of soda?



Please show works and answers!



</question>



<answer from>



Sonia D
Member since: 14 November 2007
Total points: 117 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



1)  1kg=1,000g, so you do 25 x 1,000, and the answer is 25,000 g.
2)  1L=1,000mL, so 9.3 x 1,000, and the answer is 9,300mL.
3) 1mm=1,000um, so .36 x 1,000, and the answer is 360um.
4) 1km=100,000cm, so for this one, you do 24 divided by 100,000, and the answer would either be .00024km, or 2.4 x 10 to the -4 power (if you don't understand exponents, then just write .00024)
5) 1mi=1.61km, so you do 3.4 x 1.61, and the answer is 5.474km.
6) 1lb=453.59 grams, so you do 180 x 453.49, and the answer is 81646.2 grams.
7) 1L=33.81 fluid ounces, so you do 33.81 x 3, and the answer is 101.43 fluid ounces.



</answer>

<answer from>

<answer>

Source(s):

<answer from>



Alam Ko Iyan
Member since: 20 June 2007
Total points: 73192 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



let a = 3^x
b = 2^x



notice that the equation becomes
8a^2 + 3ab - 81b^2 = 0
(a - 3b) (8a + 27b) = 0



thus



a = 3b
or  a = -27b/8



then
3^x = 3*2^x
or 3^x = (-27/8)*2^x .... this second one is not possible



thus
3^x = 3* 2^x
3^(x-1) = 2^x
get the logarithm of both sides .
(x-1) log3 = x log2
x log3 - log3 = x log2
(log3 - log2) x = log3
thus
x = log3 / (log3 - log2)
≈ 2.70951129



</answer>

<question>



Idempotent if A^2 = A.???



A square matrix A is said to be idempotent if A^2 = A.
a) Show that if A is idempotent, then so is I-A
b) Show that if A is idempotent, then 2A-I is invertible and is its own inverse.



what is idempotent??



</question>



<answer from>



nickname
Member since: 23 September 2008
Total points: 972 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



http://www.google.com/search?source=ig&h...



google is your friend.



</answer>



<answer from>



cidyah
Member since: 24 February 2007
Total points: 54238 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



a)A^2=A (given)
(I-A)^2 = I^2-2IA+A^2 = I -2A+A = I-A, so I-A is idempotent.



</answer>

<question from>



ally

<question>



How would this be factorised? 4x^2-16?



^2 means squered



</question>



<answer from>



betty swollocks
Member since: 18 October 2007
Total points: 141 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



(2x+4)(2x-4)



</answer>



<answer from>



calder28
Member since: 05 November 2007
Total points: 186 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



(2x - 4)(2x + 4)



</answer>



<answer from>



Chris L
Member since: 24 September 2008
Total points: 426 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



First, a spelling tip: "squared" instead of "squered"



This binomial is the difference of two squares.  Both 4x^2 and 16 are, individually, perfect squares:
4x^2 = (2x)(2x)
16 = (4)(4)



There is a formula you should remember for factoring when you are given the difference of two squares:
a² - b² = (a - b)(a + b)



Since a = 2x, and b = 4, this means that the binomial can be factored as:
(2x - 4)(2x + 4)



</answer>



<answer from>



JM Gendron
Member since: 08 July 2008
Total points: 2252 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



It's a difference of squares. These are very cool little equations, because, when everything is a perfect square like that, in a second degree binomial, you can simply take the square root of each: 2, x, and 4, and write:



(2x+4)(2x-4)



pull a 2 out of each



2(x+2)2(x-2)



Group your terms.



4(x+2)(x-2)



Quick and easy, if you know how to solve perfect squares.



Let's do a check. Let x=3



Original equation:



4(3)^2 -16 = ?
4(9) -16 =?
36-16=20



And the simplified equation:



4((3)+2)((3)-2)
4(5)(1) = ?



4(5) = 20



It works.



</answer>

That is called the difference of squares.

a(x-h)^2+k=0  Then the vertex is (h,k)  Since the coefficient of the x^2 term is positive this parabola will open up or hold water. This means it's decreasing on( -infinity,h) and increasing on (h, + infinity)
