<answer from>



Alen D
Member since: 30 September 2008
Total points: 124 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



You have two ways to find an answer. The one is to put it in a graph, then see where it is "increasing? decreasing?"



When a &gt; 0 then function is decreasing (-∞,-b/2a) and increasing (-b/2a, +∞).



When a &gt; 0 then function is increasing (-∞,-b/2a) and decreasing (-b/2a, +∞).



For your function, -b/2a=-3, a&gt;0, which means that function is decreasing (-∞,-3) and increasing (-3, +∞).



Source(s):



Me.



</answer>



<answer from>



funkbass...
Member since: 20 September 2008
Total points: 557 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Whether a function is increasing or decreasing can be determined by analyzing it's slope. If the slope of a function is positive, the function is increasing; if it is negative, the function is decreasing.



So, keeping that in mind, we need to analyze the slope of the given function:



f(x) = x^2 + 6x - 4 ...eq. [1]



To get the slope function of f(x), we take the first derivative of f(x) in eq. [1], which gives:



f '(x) = 2x + 6 ...eq. [2]



Now, there exist points on functions where the function is neither increasing nor decreasing. In other words, the tangent line has a horizontal slope (slope = 0). These are called critical points. Also, it is at these critical points where the function switches from increasing to decreasing (the critical point is a maximum), or vice versa (the critical point is a minimum). We need to find these points. Since the slopes at these points are equal to zero, we set eq. [2] equal to zero and solve for 'x':



2x + 6 = 0
2x = -6
x = -3



So, we only have one critical point, and that is at x = -3. So, we at least know the function switches directions (increasing/decreasing) at this point, but we don't know how exactly. To determine this, find the slope at a point to the left of x = -3 and at a point to the right of x = -3. I will use x = -10 and x = 0 for my two points. (NOTE: You can use any two points, but one has to be to the left of x = -3 and one has to be to the right of x = -3.) Evaluate the slope at these two values:



@ x = -10:
f '(-10) = 2(-10) + 6



f '(-10) = -20 + 6



f '(-10) = -14



...so, the function is decreasing to the left of x = -3.



@ x = 0:
f '(0) = 2(0) + 6
f '(0) = 0 + 6
f '(0) = 6



...so, the function is increasing to the right of x = -3.



So, to sum this up:



Decreasing: (-INFINITY, -3)
Increasing: (-3, +INFINITY)



That is how you would write your results in interval notation.



Hope this helps!



</answer>

<question>



Integration Problem Using Part 1 of Fundamental Theorem?



the integration of h(x) from [0,x^2] square root of 1+r^3 dr
I think you just use a u substitution for the x^2, is that right?



</question>



<answer from>



Alam Ko Iyan
Member since: 20 June 2007
Total points: 73193 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Yes.
d/dx ∫[0 , x^2] √(1+r^3) dr



let u = x^2
du/dx = 2x



d/dx ∫[0 , x^2] √(1+r^3) dr
= d/du * du/dx ∫[0 , x^2] √(1+r^3) dr
= {d/du ∫[0 , u] √(1+r^3) dr} * du/dx
= √(1 + u^3) * 2x
= 2x √(1 + x^6) .



</answer>

</question from>



<question>



Find the horizontal and vertical asymptotes of the curve. ?



Find the horizontal and vertical asymptotes of the curve.



y = (8 x^2 + x - 2)/(x^2 + x - 72)



</question>



<answer from>



nottheja...
Member since: 13 February 2008
Total points: 16951 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



VA: zeros of denominator (x + 9)(x - 8) ==&gt; x = -9 and x = 8



HA: limit of 8x^2 / x^2 as x ==&gt; + / - infinity
y = 8



alternatively:
divide everything by x^2
y = (8 + 1/x - 2/x^2) / (1 + 1/x - 72/x^2)
as x gets really big, 1/x and 1/x^2 get really small and tend toward 0
this leaves 8 / 1 as the end behavior as x ==&gt; +/- inf
y = 8 is the HA



*** you should also check to make sure the -9 and 8 are not zeros of the numerator (they aren't)-- that would become a removable discontinuity instead of a VA



</answer>



<answer from>



funkbass...
Member since: 20 September 2008
Total points: 559 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



y = (8x^2 + x - 2) / (x^2 + x - 72) ...eq. [1]



First, let's find the vertical asymptotes. These occur when the function has a denominator of zero. So, set the denominator of eq. [1] equal to zero, and solve for 'x':



x^2 + x - 72 = 0
(x + 9)(x - 8) = 0 ...eq. [2]



Eq. [2] is satisfied when either term on the left-hand side of the equation is equal to zero. So, set each term equal to zero, and solve for 'x':



x + 9 = 0
x = -9



x - 8 = 0
x = 8



So, at x = -9 and x = 8, there are vertical asymptotes.



Now, to find the horzontal asymptotes, compare the degree of the polynomial in the numerator to the degree of the polynomial in the denominator. The degree of the polynomial in the numerator, in this case, is the same as the degree of the polynomial in the denominator. They are both second degree. Since this is the case, we can just compare the x^2 term in the numerator and the x^2 term in the denominator while ignoring everything else.



To find the horzontal asymptote, just take the x^2 term from the numerator, and divide it by the x^2 term in the denominator. (NOTE: This only works when the polynomials in the numerator and denominator are the same!)



(8x^2) / (x^2)
= 8 / 1
= 8



So, there is a horizontal asymptote at y = 8.



Hope this helps!



</answer>

<question>



How to find square footage on a grid with two different scales?



autocad, drafting question:
I have a grid set up that is scaled:



1"=2' vertical, 1"=20' horizontal



I have a ditch that we've surveyed and plotted on this profile.  I have figured out the area of the ditch.  It comes to 1259.5543 square feet.  However, since i'm on a 2 and 20 scale, what do i need to do to get this in the correct square footage?
Thanks!



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



I'm not sure your original numbers in the reduced scale, so I'll just give an example instead.



If you had a 1" x 1 " square that would represent the following area:



(1" * 20'/1") * (1" * 2'/1") = 40 square feet



or if you had a 5"x3" square  (this is horizontal by vertical.  I'm not an engineer so I won't assume your notation is the same as mine.):



(5" * 20'/1") * (3" * 2'/1") = 600 square feet



</answer>






<original file>index;_ylt=Avhcn0rZ95B7BHCLdNJS5ydgCAx2865.html</original file>

<current file name>yqa_uk41370.txt</current file name>



<category>



Science & Mathematics



Mathematics



</category>



<question from>



cinderel...
Member since: 14 August 2007
Total points: 99 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



I have a 3.27, and i want to get at least a 3.6 is that possible this year?



i am a college student in summer semester i have 10 hours and i think i am gonna have 3 b's and 1 a (that is not averaged in with the 3.27 yet) so this FALL i am taken 18 hours IS it still possible to make a 3.6?



</question>



<answer from>



Geezah
Member since: 06 July 2006
Total points: 59922 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Religion & Spirituality



</answer from>



<answer>



Let's say your GPA for the fall is G.  Then in order for your full GPA to average out to be 3.6, you need to have (G + 3.27)/2 = 3.6.  Solving this for G gives G = 3.93.  So basically, yes it's possible, but only if you get all "A"s.



</answer>



<answer from>



cheeser1...
Member since: 18 June 2007
Total points: 20313 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Geezah is almost right, but he's not doing a weighted average like he should be...

You see, we can't really know what your GPA could be unless you tell us what your total number of hours is. For example, if you had only 20 hours total (plus 10 summer and 18 in the fall), it would be easy to bring it up. But if you had 200 hours (plus 10 plus 18), it would be much harder, because your new grades don't carry as much weight.

------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------



So let's say this: Assume you have H hours so far.

Those H hours are weighted as 3.27.
The 10 summer hours are weighted as 3.1.**
The 18 fall hours are weighted 4.0.***

**This is the "worst" case possible. You've told us "3 Bs and 1 A" but that doesn't tell us how many hours each class is. If the A is in a 2 hour class, or a 4 hour class, that's a big difference.

***This is the "best" case possible. You want to know if it's "possible" so the best you can do is a 4.0. We will use this to determine H.

------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------



So you have:

H(3.27) + 10(3.1) + 18(4) = Total Grade Points (GP)
H + 10 + 18 = Total Hours

Simplify:
GP = 3.27H + 103
Hours = H + 28

We you want:
3.6 ≤ GPA = GP / Hours



3.6 ≤ (3.27H + 103) / (H + 28)

3.6(H+28) ≤ 3.27H + 103

3.6H + 100.8 ≤ 3.27H + 103

(3.6 - 3.27)H ≤ 103 - 100.8

0.33 H ≤ 2.2

H ≤ 2.2 / 0.33 = 6.666...

So, the actual real answer to your question is:

YES if you have at most 6 hours so far (before this summer).

NO if you have more than 6 hours so far.

The fewer hours you have, the easier it will be to bring up the average, but you need 6 or fewer for it to be possible. If you get better than a 3.1 in the summer, it will also or make possible or easier your ability to bring up the average.

------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------



You can also use more variables and figure it out:

H hours are weighted as 3.27
The 10 summer hours are weighted as S
The 18 fall hours are weighted G

Now you have three variables:
H = total number of yours
S = summer GPA
G = target GPA

You still use the same equations as before, but with the new variables instead of the guesses from before:
GP = 3.27H + 10S + 18G
Hours = H + 28

You want to find the minimum possible G so that:

3.6 ≤ GPA = GP / Hours

3.6 ≤ (3.27H + 10S + 18G) / (H + 28)

3.6(H + 28) ≤ 3.27H + 10S + 18G

3.6H + 100.8 ≤ 3.27H + 10S + 18G

0.33H + 100.8 - 10S ≤ 18G

18G ≥ 0.33H + 100.8 - 10S

G ≥ 5.6 + 0.0183333H - 0.555S

Now, for this to be possible, the value of G must be bigger than the right-hand side. But notice the 5.6 -- this is what kills your chances. G cannot be that big. The only way to balance that out is to hope that your S value (summer GPA) is high enough to outweigh this (since that part is subtracted). Even then, if you have a large H value (total hours so far, before the summer), it will not be possible.

As you can see, if you get a 4.0 in the summer, you come to:

G ≥ 5.6 + 0.0183333H - 0.555(4)

G ≥ 5.6 + 0.0183333H - 2.22

G ≥ 3.38 + 0.0183333H

And to have a minimal G value of at least 4 you need:

4 = 3.38 + 0.0183333H

0.62 = 0.0183333H

H = 0.62/0.0183333 = 33.8182

At most 33 hours.

------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------



So here's a different "final answer":

If you get a 3.1 this summer, you need to get a 4.0 in the fall AND have at most 6 hours total before the summer.

If you get a 4.0 this summer, you need to get a 4.0 in the fall AND have at most 33 hours total before the summer.

------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------



If you get less than a 4.0 this fall, it becomes harder/impossible.

For example, if you get five As and just one B, that's a 3.83333333 GPA for the fall. That changes our problem to:

3.833 = 3.38 + 0.0183333H

0.453 = 0.0183333H

H = 0.453 / 0.0183333 = 24.709

You can only have at most 24 hours (instead of the 33 we said before).

------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------ ------



To give you an idea of an impossible scenario, we know that this is your goal:

G ≥ 5.6 + 0.0183333H - 0.555S

Assume you have 36 hours total, and you get a 3.7 in the summer. Is it possible to bring it up? No, because you get:

G ≥ 5.6 + 0.0183333(36) - 0.555(3.7)

G ≥ 5.6 + 0.6599988 - 2.0535

G ≥ 4.2064988

You would have to have a value of G bigger than 4.2, but the maximum possible GPA is 4.0.



</answer>

= 2p² - 12pq

<question>



How do i factor trinomial fractions? ( Algebra 2 )?



How do i factor these out, please explain ( and not make it more complicated than it has to be ) t^2 + t + 1/4  and m^2 + 2/3m + 1/9? How do i factor those? Please explain! Thank you~



</question>



<answer from>



Justin
Member since: 16 September 2008
Total points: 202 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



t^2 + t + 1/4
= (t+1/2)(t+1/2) = (t+1/2)^2

m^2 + 2/3m + 1/9
= (m+1/3)(m+1/3) = (m+1/3)^2



You factor these as you would polynomials without fractions. You look for two numbers that multiply together to get the third coefficient, and add together to get the 2nd coefficient.



</answer>



<answer from>



Jack Z
Member since: 12 January 2008
Total points: 219 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



you have to find the sqrt of 1/4 (note that square root of fractions are bigger than the product) sqrt of 1/4 is 1/2
so first question is (x+1/2)^2
next one 
m^2 + 2/3m + 1/9, sqrt of 1/9 is 1/3
(x+1/3)^2



</answer>



<answer from>



detektib...
Member since: 21 February 2006
Total points: 5683 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Factor
t^2 + t + 1/4

If the t^2 has no coefficient ( the whole number before it), you can follow these steps.

First term:  t^2 , we know that the factor of t^2 is  t  times  t

Last term : 1/4 , we know that the factor of 1/4 is  1/2 times 1/2.

Middle term : if you ADD  the 2 factors of the last term, you must get the coefficient of the middle term.

If you add 1/2t + 1/2t = 1t or t, which is the middle term.



Our factor is



( t + 1/2) ( t + 1/2)

==========

m^2 + 2/3m + 1/9 =

( m + 1/3) ( m + 1/3)



</answer>



<answer from>



Jun Agruda
Member since: 17 May 2007
Total points: 28429 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



1st algebraic expression:
t² + t + 1/4 = 0
t² + t = - 1/4
t² + 1/2t = - 1/4 + 1/2²
t² + 1/2t = - 1/4 + 1/4
(t + 1/2)² = 0
t + 1/2 = 0

Answer: (t + 1/2)² or (t + 1/2)(t + 1/2)

Proof:
= (t + 1/2)(t + 1/2)
= t² + 1/2t + 1/2t + 1/4
= t² + t + 1/4

2nd algebraic expression:
m² + 2/3m + 1/9 = 0
m² + 1/3m = - 1/9 + 1/3²
m² + 1/3m = - 1/9 + 1/9
(m + 1/3)² = 0
m + 1/3 = 0

Answer: (m + 1/3)² or (m + 1/3)(m + 1/3)

Proof:
= (m + 1/3)(m + 1/3)
= m² + 1/3m + 1/3m + 1/9
= m² + 2/3m + 1/9



</answer>

<answer>



(y-y')/y''-y')=m(x-x')/(x''-x')

where m the gradient may be deduced from the given co-ords thus
(y''-y')/(x''-x')=m

then re-arrange into the form required

maths O-level elementary class

<question>



REALLY ADVANCED SURDS question....?



A question says:
Triangle ABC has area of 5.
The length of base BC is 6sqrt2-2sqrt3.
Find the height of this triangle, measured from base BC.
Writee your answer exactly, in its simplest form.

The triangle  is obtuse.
http://mathforum.org/lucentpow/gifs/2002...



this is what is basically looks like. BC is base A is at the top, bit AC line is more stretched out..

Please explain HOW TO DO THIS!!!
Use as much detail,. please so i can fully understand, it might be long and take some time, but PLEASE!!! Most detailed answer WILL GET 13 POINTS and i will be soo grateful! PLEASE!!

Sned your time, helping me figure this monser out!!!

thanks! :)



</question>



<answer from>



Tigon
Member since: 18 June 2008
Total points: 2712 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



All you need to do is to use mensuration. Generally,

Area of triangle = 1/2 x Base x Height

So, substituting the given values,

5 = 1/2 x 6√2-2√3 x Height

Therefore rearranging we can write,

Height = 2 x 5 / (6√2-2√3)



= 10 /(6√2-2√3)



= 5 /(3√2 - √3)

We can simplify this further by rationalising the denominator. To do this multiply both the numerator and denominator of the above by 3√2 - √3, so,

= 5/(3√2 - √3)  x  (3√2 + √3) / (3√2 + √3)

= 5 (3√2 + √3) /  (3√2 - √3) (3√2 + √3)

= 5 (3√2 + √3) / 15

= 1/3(3√2 + √3)

= √2 + √3/3

=  √2 + 1/√3



</answer>



<answer from>



ReelBigF...
Member since: 17 March 2006
Total points: 162 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Well the formula for area of a triangle is (0.5 * base * height=area)
So all you need to do is plug in the stuff you know such as area and base and you just solve for height.Note that the height no matter what the triangle is perpendicular to the base.So dont let the "stretching out" confuse you.

Now lets plug in. 5=0.5*(6sqrt2 - 2sqrt3)  * height. Simplify and you get 5= height * 3sqrt2 - sqrt3. Rearrange and you have ure answer. height=5/(3sqrt2 - sqrt3)  .



</answer>



<answer from>



allenm
Member since: 05 June 2008
Total points: 2083 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Area of triangle = (1/2) * (base) * (height)

That's all you need.



area = 1/2 * base * height
height = 2 * area / base

You have 
base = 6√2 - 2√3
area = 5
height = 2 * 5 / (6√2 - 2√3)

Simplify:
2 * 5 / (6√2 - 2√3)
= [10 * (6√2 + 2√3)] / [(6√2 - 2√3) * (6√2 + 2√3)]
= (60√2 + 20√3) / [ 36*2 - 4*3 ]
= (60√2 + 20√3) / 60
= (3√2 + √3) / 3
≈ (4.243 + 3.464) / 3
≈ 7.707 / 3
≈ 2.569



</answer>

<question from>



DeviLish...
Member since: 11 June 2008
Total points: 134 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Read the Directions below and show all your work. ?



Denmark is experiencing population growth.. The Population for Denmark  in July of 2008 was 32,738,376 and it’s population growth is 0.295%.



1. Use the growth rate to approximate the population in the year 2012.



2. Show your detailed, worked out solution.



3. Write a paragraph about how you might use this information in a role as a politician, government administrator or business owner/operator.



4. What will it mean to the country, its economy, resources or the business?



5. Do not use India, China or the United states as your country. Type (1.014)^4 for (1.014) to the fourth power.



</question>



<answer from>



Michael
Member since: 08 April 2008
Total points: 1947 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Initially you might think of this as a linear function

y = mx + b

where the growth rate 
m = 0.295% = 0.0295



However think about each year...
Initially we have a population 32,738,376



After the first year we have the 100% of population + growth rate or

32,738,376  ( 1 + 0.0295)

which simplifies to
32,738,376  ( 1.0295)

Now think about the next year... 
It would be the new population + the growth rate again or...
32,738,376  ( 1.0295) ( 1.0295)



This is known as a "Geometric Progression"
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometric_p...

In a geometric progression we can write a general equation by knowing two things.  This initial value or 'a', and the rate of increase, r.

a * r ^ k

Where k is the number of times we sequence has elapsed.

In our case 
a = 32,738,376 
r = 1.0295
k = 4,



( 2012 - 2008)



So our general equation for any year will be
( 32,738,376 ) (1.0295) ^ k

Thus for k = 4 we have
( 32,738,376 ) (1.0295) ^ 4 = 36 775 834



At this rate in 2008 we could say that Denmark's population will have increased more that 4 million people in only 4 years.  If we currently had approximately 32.7 million it would mean that our population had increase by roughly 1/8 or 12 %.  This means that the country would require at a minimum 12% more resources just to keep at current pace economically.



</answer>



<asker's comment>

<answer>



It would be -10 because the signs are different. 
Think of it this way. When multiplying and dividing, it doesnt matter how huge or small the numbers are. If the signs are the same ( both positive or both negative) the answer will ALWAYS be positive. If they are different it will ALWAYs be negative. 
So once you've determined what the sign will be, just do the basic math as normal. 30 divided by 3 is 10, it must be negative, so the answer is -10!
Hope that helps!



</answer>

Part 1. find the logarithmic formula that gives the pH of a substance. State what each variable in your equation represents.

Find the pH of a substance of your choice that is alkaline (basic). Using this pH, show how to find the hydrogen ion concentration, [H+], of the substance using the formula. Discuss the meaning of pH and [H+], the pH scale and why your chosen substance is alkaline. Use scientific notation or enough decimal places so that your answer has at least 3 place values. For example, either use 3.44*10^-9 or 0.00000000344.



Part 2.
Suppose that the number of new homes built, H, in a city over a period of time, t, is graphed on a rectangular coordinate system where time is on the horizontal axis. Suppose that the number of homes built can be modeled by an exponential function, H= p * a^t , where p is the number of new homes built in the first year recorded. If you were a homebuilder looking for work, would you prefer that the value of a to be between 0 and 1 or larger than 1? Explain your reasoning.



</question>

<answer>



2) If you want to be able to build a lot of homes, then you want H to be big.  If 0 &lt; a &lt; 1, then a^t will go DOWN as t increases.  So you want a &gt; 1.



</answer>



<answer from>



nightpri...
Member since: 12 May 2008
Total points: 144 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



1) pH = -log[H+]. log has base 10. [H+] = concentration of hydrogen ions in solution. The pH of ammonia from certain fishes is around 11.45, which means that 11.45 = -log[H+], so [H+] = 10^(-11.45). This substance is alkaline because it has pH &gt; 7.0. In scientific notation, this is 3.548 * 10^(-12).

2) The home builder would want more homes available so that he can earn money. If you look at the behavior of a function with a between 0 and 1, say just Y = (a)^x, you would find that Y never stops DECREASING. This is very bad. The only option left would be larger than 1. (Why can't it be 1?)

=)

http://www.elmhurst.edu/~chm/vchembook/1...



</answer>

<question>



What is theoretical probability?



im doing a piece of maths homework and there is a question on theoretical probability and i have no idea what it means so could someone please explain it to me ?

thanks x



</question>



<additional details>



by the way, i dont get all that complicated explanations that smart people do lol. i'd like the definition for dummies lol



</additional details>



<answer from>



Cocoa Flavoured Girl
Member since: 15 August 2008
Total points: 3699 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



Theoretical probability is pretty self explanatory as a term. It is a theoretical measure of the likelihood that an event will have a particular outcome, used when the event cannot be readily tested.



For example, what is the likelihood, theoretically, that I will throw a 6 10 times when I throw the dice 100 times?



You calculate the outcome rather than stand there throwing dice all day. Also, when you think about things like theoretically, what is the probability of a black hole eating the earth, there is no way of actually doing an experiment. You have to do it theoretically, ie. on paper. (or in your head if your smart. :-)



</answer>



<answer from>



Samwise
Member since: 01 November 2007
Total points: 8635 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



The probability of an event is the proportion of a large number of experiments that it should occur. For instance, if you shuffle a standard deck of cards and randomly choose one card, it should be an ace about 1/13th of the time. That calculated probability is theoretical: it doesn't tell you whether it will happen any given time.

If you're drawing cards from a standard deck, for instance, you calculate the probability of drawing an ace under the assumption that there are four aces in the deck. That theoretical probability ought to be reliable over a large number of random draws (assuming the drawn cards are put back and the deck reshuffled each time), but it doesn't tell you when you'll get an ace or when you won't.

It also ignores the possibility that the dealer is cheating and you're getting seconds when an ace is on top of the deck, or you're cheating because you're using a marked deck.



</answer>



<answer from>



Bex
Member since: 21 May 2007
Total points: 1084 (Level 3)



</answer from>

<question>



How do you work out the median, if amount of  numbers are even and they are the same two numbers in the middle?



</question>



<answer from>



squirrel...
Member since: 31 May 2007
Total points: 10259 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



You would take the mean of the two middle numbers.  So, if they are the same number, then that would be your median.



</answer>



<answer from>



Alejo
Member since: 05 September 2008
Total points: 575 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



If there's an even number of data in the set, you take the two middle numbers, add them together, and divide by two. So obviously, if they're the same, then that number is the median.



</answer>

<answer from>



Mang109

<answer>



kk

I would

take eqn 2, rearrange to give y as the subject , y=8-x^2

substitute thats y into eqn 1



2x + 16 - 2x^2=7

use quadratic formula ( ill assume you know this, if not, ask - and someone will give it) on that nice eqn

<answer from>



intc_esc...
Member since: 13 May 2007
Total points: 2083 (Level 3)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



x² + y = 8 .................. eq1
2x + 2y = 7 ............... eq2

y = 7/2 - x ................. rearrange eq2

x² + (7/2 - x) = 8 ........ substitute eq2 into eq1
x² - x = 9/2
(x - 1/2)² = 19/4
x = (± √19 + 1)/2
x1 = (1 + √19)/2
x2 = (1 - √19)/2

y1 = 7/2 - (1 + √19)/2 . from eq2
y1 = (6 - √19)/2
y2 = (6 + √19)/2

Answer: [(1 + √19)/2, (6 - √19)/2] , [(1 - √19)/2, (6 + √19)/2]

P.S. You can clearly see that (3,1/2) does not satisfy x²+y=8 
(3)² + 1/2 = 9.5 ≠ 8



</answer>

<question>



MATHEMATICIANS! Please spare me 2 minutes!?



OK, so:



(5- sqrt11)
________
(2+ sqrt11)

How on earth does this become -3 + sqrt11 when you take the surd out of the denominator??



Thanks in advance!



</question>



<answer from>



Help
Member since: 02 December 2007
Total points: 135 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



5 - s11



x



2-s11
----------



----------
2 + s11



2- s11.........................x by conjecet

10 -7s11 + 11
--------------------



4-11

21 - 7s11
-------------
-7

= ans = -3 + s11.. ;)



</answer>



<answer from>



Elmyr
Member since: 21 July 2008
Total points: 18405 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Words & Wordplay



Trivia



</answer from>



<answer>



(5 - √11) / (2 + √11) = 
(5 - √11) * (2 - √11) / [(2 + √11)(2 - √11)] = 
(10 - 5√11 - 2√11 + 11) / (4 - 11) = 
(21 - 7√11) / -7 = 
-7 (√11 - 3) / -7 = 
√11 - 3 = 3 + √11



</answer>



<answer from>



universa...
Member since: 30 October 2007
Total points: 1197 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



[ (5 - √11)(2 - √11) ] / [ (2 + √11)(2 - √11) ]

= [10 - 5√11 -2√11 + 11] / [4 - 2√11 + 2√11 - 11]
= [21 -7√11] / (-7)
= 21/(-7) + (7√11) / 7
= -3 + √11



</answer>



<answer from>



Hasan
Member since: 17 August 2008
Total points: 232 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



(5- sqrt11)
________
(2+ sqrt11)



(5- sqrt11)(2- sqrt11)
= ----------------------------



(2+ sqrt11)(2- sqrt11)



10-5sqrt11-2sqrt11+11
= -------------------------------



4-11



21-7sqrt11
= ----------------



-7



7(3-sqrt11)
= -----------------



-7
= - 3+sqrt11
I think you get it.



</answer>

It is very roundabout, and I am sure that there are better ways of doing it, but:

for(i=0; i &lt; A; i++) {



if(A-i*B &lt; 0) {



mod = A-(i-1)*B;



break;



}
}

<question from>



Brandon C
Member since: 18 September 2008
Total points: 95 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Bernoulli probabilities?



One day your teacher surprised you with a 21-question multiple-choice quiz. Each question has 5 possible answers, only one of which is correct

If you answer the questions completely based on guessing, what is the probability that: You will answer at most 3 correctly?

i worked it out using a previous formula given to someone elses question and got .324259 but the answer was wrong, did i do this wrong or need a new formula? thanks



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Okay, it has been way too long since I did anything with probabilities, but I will certainly try to help.  After reading this problem I would lean toward a Binomial Distribution instead of a Bernoulli Distribution.  The Binomial is just a Bernoulli, but instead of a single trial (Bernoulli) we have n number of trials (Binomial).

There are a few things we must look for to determine whether this is, in fact, a Binomial Distribution:

1.  Experiment consists of a fixed number of n identical trials - This holds true, since there are 21 different trials, or guesses, in this case.

2.  Each trial can result in either a success or a failure - This is true, since there is only one correct answer for each question.

3.  Probability of success is constant from trial to trial - One answer correct out of five choices for each question, p = .2

4.  Trials are independent - Not going to prove independence here, but it should be obvious that the answer of one question does not change the probability of answering correct on a different question, if all answers are random guesses.

Since all these hold true, we will use the Binomial Distribution.

Pr(Y = y) = {n\choose y}p^y(1-p)^{n-y}

where



{n\choose k} = n!/k!(n-k)!

n = 21
y = 3
Pr(correct answer) = p = .2
Pr(incorrect answer) = 1-p = .8

Since we are not just finding the probability of getting 3 correct answers, but instead the probability of getting 3 or fewer correct, we must modify our Binomial Distribution function.  Instead we will use the Cumulative Distribution Function for the Binomial Distribution, which follows:



F(x;n,p) = \Pr(X \le x) = \sum_{i=0}^{\lfloor x \rfloor} {n\choose i}p^i(1-p)^{n-i}.



http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binomial_di...

If you feel that summations are no fun (as I do), you can just use the Initial Binomial Distribution Function given above, but do it for y = 0, y = 1, y = 2, and y = 3, then just add em up.

My answer may be horribly off, since I have never been that good at probabilities, but I got a probability of .375433.  I am pretty sure you don't use a Bernoulli though.  Hope that helped, even if it is wrong, I hope it helped you look at the problem from a little different perspective.  :-)



</answer>

<answer from>



Geezah
Member since: 06 July 2006
Total points: 72011 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Religion & Spirituality



</answer from>



<answer>



If you mean sin^2(θ) - 1 = cos^2(θ), and not sin(2θ) - 1 = cos(2θ), or sin(2θ - 1) = cos(2θ), or some other combination, then

sin^2(θ) - 1 = cos^2(θ)
sin^2(θ) - (sin^2(θ)+cos^2(θ)) = cos^2(θ)
-cos^2(θ) = cos^2(θ)
The only way a value can be its own negative is if it's equal to 0.  So
cos^2(θ) = 0
cos(θ) = 0
θ = pi/2, 3pi/2, etc.



</answer>



<answer from>



Upward Bound Precalc Tutor
Member since: 09 May 2008
Total points: 4246 (Level 4)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



If sin 2Θ - 1 = cos 2Θ
It must be true that
2sinΘcosΘ - 1 = 2cos² Θ - 1
so add 1 to both sides
2sinΘcosΘ = 2cos² Θ 
divide both sides by 2
sinΘcosΘ = cos² Θ 
Set this equal to zero
cos² Θ  - sin Θ cos Θ = 0
factor cos Θ from all terms
cos Θ [ cos Θ - sin Θ]  = 0
and we set each factor to zero to determine
solution set presumably on [0, 2π)

Now cos Θ = 0 implies that Θ = π/2 or 3π/2 {90° and 270° if you like to think in degrees, calculus uses radians, however}
and  cos Θ - sin Θ = 0 ↔ cos Θ = sin Θ



and that is satisfied in the first and third quadrants at
 Θ = π/4 or 5π/4 {45° and 225° are degree equivelents, but use radians}
Complete solution set on [0,2π) is  π/4 π/2 5π/4 3π/2
--------------------------------------...
I solved this assuming you meant exactly what you typed, not sin² Θ - 1 = cos² Θ  as some of the 
other answers are assuming
If you did intend sin 2Θ to mean sin² Θ 
I would expect you to write (sin theta)^2 
or, at least sin^2 theta {less preferable but OK}
as sin² Θ means (sin Θ)²



</answer>

<question>



How do you find the area of a sector of an ellipse?



I know the equation of the ellipse (x^2 over a^2 plus y^2 over b^2 = 1)(a= 4, b=3) and the angle of the sector (45degrees). I think it's something to do with integration but i'm unsure so any help would be appreciated!



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



In Polar coordinates, sector area = integral radius * d(angle) from start angle to end angle.



Here radius = sqrt(x^2 + y^2)



</answer>

<question>



Prove that A intersect B = an empty set IFF (if and only if) A is a subset of B.?



and prove its converse.



</question>



<additional details>



Its true, I just need it proven, either by contradiction, contrapostive, or any other method.



</additional details>



<answer from>



a²+b²=c²
Member since: 15 May 2006
Total points: 3811 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



This is not true. If A is a subset of B then A intersect B is A. For example, let A = {1, 2} and B = {1, 2, 3}. A is a subset of B and A intersect B is A is not the empty set.



</answer>

<question from>



lovemybr...
Member since: 03 July 2007
Total points: 541 (Level 2)



</question from>



<question>



The rational function is G(x)=7x^2-6x-1/x^2-1. As x approaches -infinity, what is G(x)? Please help!?



I'm stuck on this on question. All help is appreciated :)



</question>



<additional details>



Is that for negative infinity?



</additional details>



<answer from>



mohanrao d
Member since: 08 August 2006
Total points: 26632 (Level 7)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



[7x^2 - 6x - 1] /(x^2-1)

=(7x+1)(x-1)/(x+1)(x-1)

=(7x+1)/(x+1)

lim x---&gt;∞ (7x+1)/(x+1) = ∞/∞, since it is indeterminate form apply

L'Hopital's rule

lim x ---&gt;∞  derivative of (7x+1) / derivative of (x+1) = 7/1 = 7



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Thank you so much! It was correct! :)



</asker's comment>

<question>



Pre-Calculus Question Help!?



OK so, I've stared at my math book dozens of times and repeated the steps it said... its obviously on crack because i take those steps and still get the wrong answers... so there's 2 i need help with

1- Product of two trinomials - (using vertical format) Find the product of:



(-x^2 + x - 5) (3x^2 + 4x +1)

2- Product of two trinomials - Find the product of:

[(m - 3) + n] [(m - 3) - n]



And try to explain each step please, I'm not very good at math :[ , i have a test tomorrow so i need to get this down ASAP, Much appreciated for help.



</question>



<answer from>



twilight...
Member since: 17 September 2007
Total points: 1422 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



1.  (-x^2 + x - 5) (3x^2 + 4x +1)
distribute going from one parenthesis to the next. (ex: -x^2(3x^2+4x+1)) and do it for all the terms.
-3x^4 -4x^3 -x^2 + 3x^3 + 4x^2 +x -15x^2 -20x -5
simplify
-3x^4 -x^3 -12x^2 -19x -5

2. [(m-3) +n] [(m-3)-n]
distribute
(m-3)(m-3)-n(m-3)+n(m-3)-n^2
do a little simplifying
(m-3)^2 -n^2
more simplifying
m^2-6m+9-n^2

good luck on your test ^_^



</answer>

</asker's comment>



<answer from>



original...
Member since: 01 July 2006
Total points: 3559 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



(-x^2 + x - 5) (3x^2 + 4x +1) = -3x^4 -4x^3 -x^2 +3x^3 +4x^2 +x
-15x^3 -20x - 5

simplifying (adding common terms)

............  = -3x^4 -16x^3 + 3x^2 - 19x -5

[(m - 3) + n] [(m - 3) - n] = (m-3+n)(m-3-n) = m^2 -3m -mn -3m -9 -3n + nm -3n -n^2

simplifying (adding common terms)

.................. = m^2 - 6m - 6n - n^2



</answer>



<answer from>



Rob H
Member since: 16 September 2007
Total points: 600 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



just try to simplify it.
for instance, if you had 
(a + b + c) * (d + e + f) what would you do?

you would do

'a' times everything in the second bracket, then 'b' times everything in the second bracket, and same for 'c'.

i.e. you'd get 
a(d+e+f) + b(d+e+f) + c(d+e+f)

do you follow?

so it's just the same for these.

i.e.
(-x^2 + x - 5) (3x^2 + 4x +1) 
=(-x^2)(3x^2 + 4x + 1) + (x)(3x^2 + 4x + 1) + (-5)(3x^2 + 4x + 1).

then expand that out and simplify, a simple exercise but lengthy so i won't do it here.



the same is true for your second problem, but note that the extra brackets do not make any difference.



</answer>

<question>



Find the equations in standard form of the following conics?



A) the ellipse with centre (2,3), a major axis of length 8, and an endpoint of the minor axis at (5,3)

B) the hyperbola with centre (0,0) if one vertex is at (0,2) and one asymptote is  y= 1/3 x



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



(x - 2)/rt 8 + (y - 3)/rt 3 = 1

(x)/rt rt 2/3 + (y)/rt 2 = 1



</answer>

<answer>



x= 2 rt(y-1)^(1/3)
 2x= rt(y-1)^(1/3)
 4x^2 = (y-1)^(1/3)
 (4x^2)^3 = y - 1



64 x^6 +1 = y

<answer from>



kentucky...
Member since: 02 September 2007
Total points: 698 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



1 kg



*



(1000 grams/1kg)*(1 peso/ 15 grams) =  66.67 pesos



(in this case I guess I'd say 66 pesos since you can't have 0.67 of a coin, so you round down)

Learn this format of converting units ("for every 1 kg, there is 1000 grams, and for every 15 grams, there's one peso").



It comes up alot in chemistry and practically every other science class.



Anyhow, also note how the units cancel each other out until you're just left with the units of the answer....pesos.



Not only is this a way to solve a problem, but a good way to check it as well to see if you forgot anything along the way.



</answer>

<question>



I need help on some probability questions that are true/false!?



For 2 events A and B, P(A)=.70, P(B|A)=.50 [Probability of B occuring, given that A has occured], and that A and B are independent events. for each of the following statements, decide if they are true, false, or can't tell, and explain why.

a) A and B are mutually exclusive.
b) A and (A U B) [A or B] are independent.
c) P(B) = P(A|B) [Probability of A given B has occured)
d) P(A|B)&lt;P(B|A)
e) P(B)&lt; or equal to P(A)



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



a) If A and B are independent, they cannot be mutually exclusive.
b) A and (A U B) are not mutually exclusive, so they must be independent.
c) False. They are different values.
d) False. 0.7 = P(A|B) &gt; P(B|A) = 0.5.
e) True. Values are given.



</answer>

<question>



This probability question is really giving me trouble... need help!?



An insurance company classifies people into one of the 3 categories; good risk, average risk, and bad risk. Historical data shows that the probability of a good risk person getting into an accident over a one year span is .05, for an average risk person it is .15, and for a bad risk person the probability is .30. Suppose that 20% of the people are good risk, 50% are average risk, and 30% are bad risk.

-what fraction of the population is involved in an accident in any one year?
- If Joe(a policy holder) had no accidents in 2005, what is the probability that Joe is a good risk person?
- what is the probability that he is an average risk person?



</question>



<answer from>



Jeff
Member since: 14 February 2006
Total points: 298 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Make a chart:

Good w/ acc: .01 Good w/o acc: .19
Avg w/ acc: .075 Avg w/o acc: .425
Bad w/ acc: .09 Bad w/o acc: .21



1) .01 + .075 + .09 = .175

2) 1-.175 = .825 did not have an accident
.19/ .825 = .2303...

3).425/.825 = .5151...



</answer>



<answer from>



mojoloco
Member since: 22 July 2008
Total points: 403 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



You must bear in mind that all of these numbers a re probabilities, not certainties.

For your for you first question. Take the sum of the products of the probabilities and the percentages (decimal):



(.05)(.2) + (.15)(.50) +(.3)(.3) =



.01 + .075 + ,09 =  0.175



If Joe had no accidents the probability that he is a good risk person
is 1 minus the probability that he is not a good risk person..  That probability, from the answer to question 1 is 1 - ,075 - .09 = .0.8835



The probability that Joe is an average risk person is 1 minus the probability that he is not average risk person. Again, from the answer to question 1, that probability is 1 - .01 -.09  = 0.9



</answer>

<question>



Word Problem Find the percent increase Please help!!?



Hi everyone I've been stuck on this problem forever if somone could help me i would really appreciate it! Here's the problem. By what percent did daily offshore oil production increase from 1960 to 2000 if in 
1960 it was: 319
1970 it was: 1577
1980 it was: 1034
1990 it was: 1082
and in 2000 it was: 1741
Round to the nearest tenth. Thank you all!!



</question>



<answer from>



SAT Girl
Member since: 15 September 2008
Total points: 231 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



The percent increase can be found using the forumal is/of =%/100

So the increase is 1422.

We want to know what percent 1422 is of 319.



So you get

1422/319= %

1422/319= 4.45768

445.768%

Rounded is 445.8%

The poster above made a msitake in calculation and divided the original by the increase instead of the increase by the original.



</answer>

<answer>



The percent increase is the amount of increase divided by the original amount (times 100%).
Amount of increase: (1741-319)=1422
Original amount: 319
% increase: 319/1422=.224 or 22.4%

<question>



Ln 4 - 2ln(x+1) = ln x?



How would I go about solving this equation for x? I'm not just looking for the answer, more how to work through it and what rules I need to use to arrive at the answer.



</question>



<answer from>



phoenixs...
Member since: 22 February 2008
Total points: 29682 (Level 7)



</answer from>



<answer>



ln 4-2 ln(x+1)=ln(4/(x+1))=ln (x)



4/(x+1)=x



4=x^2+x



x^2+x-4=0



use the quadratic formula to solve the result



</answer>



<answer from>



azred_tx
Member since: 07 June 2007
Total points: 8954 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



Rearrange to get ln x + 2ln(x+1) - ln 4 = 0

Recall that ln(a) - ln(b) = ln (a/b), ln(a) + ln(b) = ln(ab), and a*ln(b) = ln(b^a).

ln{[x*(x+1)^2]/4} = 0

Exponentiate both sides to get

[x*(x+1)^2]/4 = 1

Now convert into a cubic equation and solve normally.



</answer>



<answer from>



mohanrao d
Member since: 08 August 2006
Total points: 26632 (Level 7)



</answer from>



<answer>



ln 4 - 2ln(x+1) = ln x

ln 4 - ln(x+1)^2 = ln x (since a ln b = ln b^a)

ln [4 /(x+1)^2] = ln x ( since ln a - ln b = ln (a/b))

take out logs

4/(x+1)^2 = x

4 = x (x^2 + 2x + 1)

x^3 + 2x^2 + x - 4 = 0

x^3 + 3x^2 + 4x - x^2 - 3x - 4 = 0

x(x^2 + 3x + 4) - 1(x^2 + 3x + 4) = 0

(x - 1)(x^2 + 3x + 4) = 0

x = 1 (ignoring imaginary roots)



</answer>

<question>



Mathematicians HELP ME!!!?



3-sqrt3
______
4+sqrt5

I'm told I should be able to get rid of the sqrt as the denominator, so it should be:

(3-sqrt3)(4-sqrt5)
_______________



11

How the hell? I understand the whole thing about multiplying the top by the bottom (making it negative, so 4-sqrt5 first) but I dont know how to get 11. Please help!



</question>



<additional details>



Thanks so much everyone I've got it now but I wouldn't have without your kind help :)



</additional details>



<answer from>



phoenixs...
Member since: 22 February 2008
Total points: 29682 (Level 7)



</answer from>



<answer>



(4+sqrt(5))(4-sqrt(5))=16-5=11



</answer>



<answer from>



lt;
Member since: 27 November 2006
Total points: 1532 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



multiply numerator and denominator by (4-sqrt5)

so denominator u get (4+sqrt5)(4-sqrt5)

as (a+b)(a-b) = a^2 - b^2

we get (4^2 - (sqrt5)^2)
which is (4^2 - 5)
which is 16-5 =11



</answer>



<answer from>



david536...
Member since: 27 December 2006
Total points: 6230 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



Multiply (3-sqrt3)/(4+sqrt5) by (4-sqrt5)/(4-sqrt5)

then the denominator becomes (4+sqrt5)(4-sqrt5)
multiply it out and you get 16 +4sqrt5 - 4sqrt5 - (sqrt5)(sqrt5)
which equals 16 - 5 = 11



</answer>



<answer from>



Element
Member since: 03 September 2008
Total points: 1519 (Level 3)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



Since you know you're multiplying by 4-sqrt5, you have a difference of 2 squares in the denominator:

(4+sqrt5)(4-sqrt5)

Multiply that out and you get:

4^2 - (sqrt5)^2 =
16 - 5 =
11



</answer>



<answer from>



jimbot
Member since: 19 June 2008
Total points: 1203 (Level 3)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



(3 - √3) / (4 + √5)

= (3 - √3)(4 - √5) / (4 + √5)(4 - √5)
= (3 - √3)(4 - √5) / 11

recall that (x + a)(x - a) = x² - a², so

(4 + √5)(4 - √5)
= 4² - √5²
= 16 - 5 = 11



</answer>



<answer from>



MrScienc...
Member since: 31 December 2007
Total points: 127 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



multiply your original equation by "a well chosen one"
I choose [you should too]



(4-sqrt5)
------------
(4-sqrt5)

the numerator is as you show it.
the denominator is
(4 + sqrt5)(4 - sqrt5)
expands to:
16 + 4sqrt5 - 4sqrt5 - sqrt5sqrt5
middle two terms cancel last term simplifies to 5
16 - 5 = 11

full answer is as you showed.



</answer>

lenpol7
Member since: 25 November 2006

</answer from>



<answer>



Yes you are correct about using the conjugate (4 - sqrt5)



(3-sqrt3)



x  ( 4 - sqrt5)
_________________ 
(4+sqrt5)



x ( 4 - sqrt5)

The terms are multiplied together
(3-sqrt3)



x  ( 4 - sqrt5)

Remember FOIL
Numerator:-
12 -4sqrt3 - 3sqrt5 + sqrt(15)

Denominiator
(4+sqrt5)



x ( 4 - sqrt5)

16 - 4sqrt5 + 4sqrt5 - sqrt(25)
16 - sqrt25
16 - 5 
11 - THE '11' in your answer!!!!!!
NB :-
- 4sqrt5 + 4sqrt5 these two terms are the same value, but one is positive and the other negative and so eliminate each other.

<answer>



You can't prove it, because it isn't true.

However, here is a link to what you are probably looking for:

http://www.moillusions.com/2008/02/anoth...

This doesn't prove that 5x13 = 8x8--it's just an illusion. If you cut an 8x8 rectangle as shown and rearrange the pieces to make the 5x13 rectangle, then the 5x13 rectangle will have a very small hole down the diagonal (the pieces do not line up exactly). The area of the hole will be 1 square unit, but it's spread over a long ways so it's not very noticeable.



</answer>

<question>



How do you work out this equation?



9 (to the power of y)/ 27 (to the power of 2y +1) = 81

Find y.



</question>



<answer from>



sasygoma...
Member since: 17 September 2008
Total points: 227 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>

</answer>



<answer from>



NeedUrHe...
Member since: 09 January 2008
Total points: 2747 (Level 4)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



9^y / 27^(2y + 1) = 81
(3^2)^y / (3^3)^(2y + 1) = 3^4
3^2y / 3^(6y + 3) = 3^4
3^2y / (3^6y * 3^3) = 3^4
3^2y / 3^6y = 3^4 * 3^3
3^(-4y) = 3^7
-4y = 7
y = -7/4 Answer



</answer>



<answer from>



aravindm...
Member since: 22 September 2006
Total points: 748 (Level 2)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



9=3^2  and 27=3^3

so equation is (3^2)^y / (3^3)2y+1 =81
3^2y/3^6y+3=81

3^2y-6y-3 =81

3^-4y-3=81



81=3^4

so -4y-3=4

so y=-7/4



</answer>



<answer from>

81 = 3^4

3^2y / 3^6y +3 = 3^4

2y - 6y +3 = 4

-4y = 7

y = -7/4

<question>



Help me in limits question?



A 120 yards foot ball field to be marked by using measuring stick that is approximately 6 yard long. How close tot 6 yrds must the measuring stick be to ensure that the actual lenght  of the field --- yrds of 120

Actual length of stick.....
Actual length of field....
Epcialone .....
Delta .........



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Denote length of stick by x, length of marked field by y.  Then
y = 20x

Let me use d for delta and e for epsilon.
We require
|120 - y| &lt; d
i.e.
-d &lt; 120 - y &lt; d
i.e.
-d &lt; 120 - 20x &lt; d

Divide each term by 20:
-d/20 &lt; 6 - x &lt; d/20

Thus x must be within e of 6 yards where
 e = d/20



</answer>

<question>



Differential equations question?



Solve y' = 4(x^2)(y^2)
y(1) = -1

Also find the existence interval



</question>



<answer from>



kuiperbe...
Member since: 16 December 2007
Total points: 16911 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Physics



</answer from>



<answer>



this is a separable variable equation:

dy/y^2 = 4x^2 dx

-1/y = 4/3 x^3+C

when x=1, y=-1 or:

1=4/3+C =&gt; C=-1/3

1/y = 1/3(1-4x^3)

or y=3/(1-4x^3)  this has critical points when x=(1/4)^(1/3)



</answer>



<answer from>



Geezah
Member since: 06 July 2006
Total points: 72011 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



Religion & Spirituality



</answer from>



<answer>



This is separable:
dy / dx = 4(x^2)(y^2)
y^-2 dy = 4x^2 dx

Integrate both sides to get
-y^(-1) = (4/3)x^3 + C

Plug in x=1, y=-1 to solve for C



</answer>



<answer from>



Justin
Member since: 16 September 2008
Total points: 202 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



y'=dy/dx=4(x^2)(y^2)
y^-2 dy = 4x^2 dx (integrate both sides)
-y^-1 = (4/3)x^3 + c
-1/y = (4/3)x^3 + c
y=-1/((4/3)x^3 + c) ******

y(1)=-1=-1/((4/3)1^3 + c)
-1=-1/((4/3)+c)
4/3+c=1
c=-1/3 (Plug back into stared equation)
Answer: y=-1/((4/3)x^3 -1/3)

Theres problems when:
(4/3)x^3 -1/3=0
(4/3)x^3 =1/3
x^3=1/4
So x can't equal the cubed root of .25



</answer>

<answer from>



H2O Engineer
Member since: 24 July 2008
Total points: 2511 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



I believe it should be rounded to 42 see explanation below and examples.



Common method
This method is commonly used in mathematical applications, for example in accounting. It is the one generally taught in elementary mathematics classes. This method is also known as Symmetric Arithmetic Rounding or Round-Half-Up (Symmetric Implementation)

Decide which is the last digit to keep. 
Increase it by 1 if the next digit is 5 or more (this is called rounding up) 
Leave it the same if the next digit is 4 or less (this is called rounding down) 
Examples:

3.044 rounded to hundredths is 3.04 (because the next digit, 4, is less than 5). 
3.045 rounded to hundredths is 3.05 (because the next digit, 5, is 5 or more). 
3.0447 rounded to hundredths is 3.04 (because the next digit, 4, is less than 5). 
For negative numbers the absolute value is rounded and the sign is added back afterwards.



</answer>

<question>



Ok so i'm 25, and I need to refresh up on some of my math. Solve and explain this problem so I can understand?



Janette took out a college loan of $20,000 with an annual interest rate of 2%. Assuming she doesn’t pay any of it back, how much money will she owe in 5 years if the interest is compounded annually?



</question>



<answer from>



Ryan P
Member since: 18 September 2008
Total points: 103 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



so you use the starting value (20,000) and multiply by the interest rate (1+.02) and the number of years as an exponent (5)
so y=20000(1.02)^5
so she would owe $22,082



</answer>



<answer from>



Brandon
Member since: 14 September 2008
Total points: 434 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Formula for compound interest

P(1 + R/100)^n

where P is the Principle amount

R is the rate

N is the number of years

Answer is

20000( 1 + 2/100) ^5 = 22081.61606
= 22081.61 (nearest cent)

Hope you have had all your queries cleared.



</answer>



<answer from>



No Longer Dizzy
Member since: 05 July 2007
Total points: 5469 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



With a low number of years like 5, you could simply use a calculator and find 2 percent of 20,000 (well, you can do this without a calculator - it's 400) and add it on, giving 20,400, then 2 percent of this is 408, add it, giving 20,808, then 2 percent of this is 416.16, add it, giving 21224.16, the 2 percent of this is  424.48, add it, giving 21648.64, then 2 percent of this is 432.97, add it, giving 22,081.61 dollars.

But this takes ages, and you could never do it with a greater time period.  There is a formula which you can use to go straight to the answer.  It looks complicated at first, but is simple.  Here it is.

Initial amount (1 + r/100)^n

Your initial amount is 20,000, and your rate is 2 and the n at the end is 5.

So find the bit in brackets first.  1 + 2/100

The answer is 1 + 0.02, which is 1.02

Now you have to raise it to the power of 5.  You need a scientific calculator.  Get your answer and then multiply it by your initial amount of 20,000, giving 22081.62 dollars.

Notice that there is a cent of difference when calculating it this way.  This is because this formula allows for more exactness as you avoid rounding inaccuracies.

It's very difficult to demonstrate this kind of formula on the pc, but I'll give you a link to a site.  This site gives explanations and examples for a lot of maths topics.  It will help a lot in your revision of maths.

First click on schools, then lessons, then secondary.  You will then be given a choice of key stage 3 maths or key stage 4 maths.  You might like to start with key stage 3 if you have forgotten a lot.  It's ages 11 - 14.  Key stage 4 is for 14-16 yrs.  You have to register to access the lessons, but it's free.

Good luck.

http://www.hotcourses.com/community/home...



</answer>

<question>



A sequence starts 11, 19, 27, 35, 43.... Find the nth term of this sequence?



:):) please help me. its due in tommorow :O



</question>



<answer from>

<answer from>



Twisted Transistor
Member since: 16 September 2008
Total points: 130 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



"8n+3" is the formula  so the next term would be 51,59,67 etc.



</answer>



<answer from>



cutolo13...
Member since: 10 October 2007
Total points: 451 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



The nth term is 3 + n x 8.



</answer>



<answer from>



Bobbin
Member since: 17 April 2007
Total points: 2359 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Let's take any two consecutive values in that sequence and subtract them:
19-11 = 8
(Check: 27-19 also = 8)

So this means we have '8n'.
But, of course, this is not right... (e.g. 8n - n=1, first term is not 8!)
So we need to adjust 8n to make it fit into the sequence.
So, the nth term is '8n+3'
(Try it out! It works :))



</answer>



<answer from>



SAM B
Member since: 17 December 2007
Total points: 107 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



8n+3



</answer>



<answer from>



amy
Member since: 23 November 2007
Total points: 1237 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



It's 8n+3.
To find the nth term you just work out how much the numbers differ, in this case it is 8. So you know it is 8n. Then you just figure out how much you have to add to each number to reach each number in the sequence. In this case, +3.
So it comes out as 8n+3. :-)
xxx



</answer>
